**`pyproject.toml:88–92` — no `addopts` or `filterwarnings` in `[tool.pytest.ini_options]`.**
The test report output is described as "pristine," but `pytest-asyncio&gt;=0.23` is known to emit `PytestUnraisableExceptionWarning` and deprecation notices in some configurations when `asyncio_mode = "auto"` is active and no `filterwarnings` block is set. This is speculative — the GREEN phase output shown in the report is clean — but it is worth adding `filterwarnings = ["error"]` once the suite grows, to catch warnings-as-errors early. Minor cosmetic/future-proofing concern; not a defect for this task.

**`docker-compose.yml` — no `restart` policy on the `api` service.**
If the API container exits before Postgres finishes initializing (edge case given `service_healthy`, but possible on very slow hosts), it will not restart. Not a blocking issue for a dev stack, but `restart: on-failure` is a common hardening step.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`src/fold_at_scripps/api/health.py:41` — `# noqa: B008` is missing the required explanatory comment.**

```python
async def readiness(session: AsyncSession = Depends(get_session)) -&gt; dict[str, str]:  # noqa: B008
```

The project rule states: *"do not add `# type: ignore`/suppressions without a specific error code AND a comment explaining why."* The suppression carries `B008` (the specific error code — correct), but has no inline explanation of why. The report's rationale ("canonical FastAPI dependency injection pattern") belongs on the line, not only in the report. The fix is one-line:

```python
async def readiness(session: AsyncSession = Depends(get_session)) -&gt; dict[str, str]:  # noqa: B008 — FastAPI Depends() in a default arg is the canonical DI pattern; B008 is a false positive here
```

This is an explicit project constraint, not a style preference. The suppression is technically correct and minimal; the error code is present; only the inline explanation is missing.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`tests/conftest.py:146` — `_reset_db_singletons` is `autouse=True` globally, running for every test including non-async unit tests.**

The fixture is an `Iterator[None]` (synchronous), so it does not cause errors in non-async tests, and the null assignments are essentially free. But future readers may wonder why the DB module is being mutated for config-only tests. Scoping it to the `integration` marker (or to `tests/test_db.py` and `tests/api/`) would be more precise. This is a cosmetic point — the current form is correct and causes no failures.

**`src/fold_at_scripps/db.py:86–89` — `get_session` declared `async def` but typed as returning `AsyncIterator[AsyncSession]`, with no `@asynccontextmanager`.**

This is valid FastAPI generator-dependency syntax: an `async def` with `yield` implicitly creates an async generator. FastAPI handles it correctly. However, the return annotation `AsyncIterator[AsyncSession]` is technically imprecise — the actual type is `AsyncGenerator[AsyncSession, None]`, which is a subtype of `AsyncIterator`. In practice this causes no runtime issue and mirrors the spec's verbatim code, so it is not a defect introduced by this implementer. Noting it for awareness only.

The implementation is correct, complete, and minimal. The `_reset_db_singletons` deviation is justified, correctly diagnosed, and minimal. For the current test suite this is harmless (pytest-asyncio's event loop teardown will GC the engine and close connections), but it can surface "Event loop is closed" warnings in asyncio debug mode. This is a very minor quality concern, not a correctness defect.

### Strengths

- **Clean, idiomatic foundation.** Every module has `from __future__ import annotations`, Google-style docstrings, full type hints, and absolute imports — consistent with the plan's global constraints and the user's style guide. `config.py:10-22`, `db.py`, `main.py`, `health.py` are all tidy and minimal.
- **Lazy singleton DB layer is the right call.** `db.py:18-26` defers engine creation until first use, so importing the package (e.g. for `--help` or unit tests that never touch the DB) never opens a connection. `pool_pre_ping=True` is a sound default for a long-lived service that will face transient Postgres disconnects.
- **Integration tests verify real behavior.** `test_db.py:12-15` and the readiness test in `test_health.py:19-25` both hit a real Postgres through a real `ASGITransport`/session — nothing is mocked. The `integration` marker plus CI's Postgres service means these actually exercise connectivity in CI (`ci.yml:90-103` sets `FOLD_DATABASE_URL` and runs unfiltered `pytest -v`).
- **The `_reset_db_singletons` fixture (conftest.py:19-32) is a justified, well-documented deviation.** Its docstring correctly explains the event-loop-binding problem: pytest-asyncio creates a fresh loop per test, and a module-level engine created under a prior (now-closed) loop would break. Resetting the globals is the correct fix and the seam is clean. This is a real improvement over the brief's file list, not scope creep.
- **`extend-immutable-calls` (pyproject.toml:35-46) is cleaner than the `# noqa: B008` it replaced** and pre-registers all FastAPI injectors, so future endpoints using `Query`/`Body`/etc. won't trip B008. Forward-looking without being speculative code.
- **CI and Compose are faithful to the plan** and share the same Postgres credentials/healthcheck, so local and CI environments match.

### Minor-findings triage

- **[T1] `test_settings_defaults` doesn't assert `database_url` default** — *defer (low value).* The env-read test already covers `database_url`; asserting the hardcoded default adds little and couples the test to a literal. Optional one-liner if desired.

- **[T2] `TestClient` constructed inline** — *defer.* Fine at two tests; promote to a fixture when the API suite grows.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)
None. The foundation is correct and boots; tests verify real behavior.

#### Important (Should Fix)

- **CI has no Python version pin — `ci.yml:92-97`.** `setup-uv@v5` with no `python-version` resolves whatever interpreter is on the runner/uv default, while the developer ran 3.14.x (per T5 note) and the Dockerfile pins `python:3.11-slim`. Three different Python versions across dev / CI / runtime is exactly the drift a foundation plan should foreclose, and a 3.11-vs-3.14 mismatch can mask version-specific failures until a later plan trips on them. *Fix:* pin `setup-uv` with `python-version: "3.11"` (or add `.python-version`), matching the Dockerfile and `requires-python`. Cheap, and it makes CI faithful to the deployment target. (I'd actually rate this borderline Critical for a "tested foundation every later plan builds on," but it doesn't break the current build, so Important.)

- **Readiness endpoint returns 500, not 503, when the DB is down — `health.py:21-24`.** `await session.execute(text("SELECT 1"))` raises on connection failure, which FastAPI surfaces as an unhandled 500. A readiness probe's contract is "return non-2xx (conventionally 503) when not ready" — orchestrators (k8s, the planned scheduler/deploy) distinguish 503 from 500. As written, an unreachable DB looks like an application crash rather than "not ready yet." *Assessment:* the plan only specified the happy path and no test covers the failure case, so this is faithful to the brief — but it's a foundation seam that later plans (health-gated deploys) will build on, so I'd fix it now: wrap in `try/except` and raise `HTTPException(status_code=503, detail="database unavailable")`, with a non-integration test asserting 503 against a bad `FOLD_DATABASE_URL`. At minimum, flag it explicitly for the deployment plan.

- **Test output is *not* fully pristine: recurring StarletteDeprecationWarning.** Per T2 this comes from FastAPI's bundled `TestClient` (a dependency), not project code, so it cannot be silenced by fixing our code. *Assessment:* acceptable to merge — it's third-party and the only sync-client test is `test_liveness`. But do **not** add `filterwarnings = ["error"]` until it's resolved (it would fail the suite). Best low-cost mitigation if you want clean output: a narrowly-scoped `filterwarnings` ignore in `pyproject.toml` keyed to that specific warning/module, with a comment, rather than a global suppression. Defer is fine; just don't lose track of it.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

- **No graceful engine disposal anywhere — `db.py` / `main.py`.** There's no FastAPI `lifespan`/shutdown hook calling `await get_engine().dispose()`, and the test fixture (conftest.py:30-32) drops the engine reference without disposing it. Harmless at this scope (process exit reclaims sockets), but a lifespan shutdown is the natural home for clean pool teardown and will be wanted once real DB work lands. Add an `await engine.dispose()` in the conftest teardown and a `lifespan` shutdown handler in a later plan.
- **`integration`-marked tests fail (not skip) when Postgres is absent — conftest.py / pyproject.toml:23-26.** The marker is registered but nothing auto-skips it without a DB. A developer following the README who forgets `docker compose up -d postgres` gets red failures, not informative skips. Consider a `pytest_collection_modifyitems` hook (or a `--run-integration` opt-in) that skips integration tests when `FOLD_DATABASE_URL` is unreachable/unset. Documented in the README, so low severity, but it's a friction point for a repo many people will clone.
- **`api` Compose service bind-mounts `./src` but the image was built with deps installed, not the source as editable in a way that reflects live edits to deps** — `docker-compose.yml:23-24`. Live-reload of `src` works, but there's no `--reload` flag on the container `CMD` (Dockerfile:15), so edits to mounted `src` won't actually hot-reload in the container. Minor dev-ergonomics gap; either add `--reload` for the compose dev target or document that the container needs a restart on edits.

### Recommendations (later plans / process)

- **Data-model plan:** introduce a SQLAlchemy declarative `Base` and an Alembic setup; the lazy-engine seam here is ready for it. Add the `lifespan` shutdown disposal at the same time.
- **Deployment plan:** multi-stage Dockerfile with `--no-dev`, `restart: on-failure`, the 503 readiness contract, and the CI Python pin (if not done now) all belong together. The current single-stage image and dev-dep install are correctly deferred.
- **Process:** the per-task ledger in `progress.md` worked well — the Minor findings were accurate and well-triaged. Keep that pattern.

### Assessment

**Ready to merge?** With fixes.

**Reasoning:** The foundation is correct, idiomatic, and its tests verify real behavior against real Postgres — no Critical issues. Before merge I'd pin the CI Python version (cheap, prevents the dev/CI/runtime version drift a foundation must avoid) and decide on the 503 readiness contract (fix now or explicitly defer to the deployment plan); everything else is safely deferrable.</result>

### Strengths

The implementation is a clean, faithful transcription of the brief. `str_enum` correctly combines `native_enum=False` with `values_callable=lambda cls: [member.value for member in cls]`, guaranteeing that enum member values (not names) are written to the VARCHAR column and appear in the CHECK constraint — the key correctness requirement. The `NAMING_CONVENTION` dict covers exactly the five Alembic-standard keys with the correct SQLAlchemy interpolation tokens; the `Base.metadata` assignment follows the recommended pattern for Alembic compatibility. `TimestampMixin` correctly uses `server_default` (not Python-side `default`) for both columns and `onupdate` for `updated_at`, ensuring DB-side time generation. The `length=max(...)` in `str_enum` is a thoughtful addition that right-sizes the VARCHAR column without being asked. Test coverage directly exercises the contract properties (`native_enum is False`, `enums == [...]`, naming-convention key set, enum value equality and ordering).

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`base.py:75` — `UUIDPKMixin` mapped column annotation on a plain class**

The mixin class `UUIDPKMixin` is a plain Python class (not inheriting from `Base`). The `Mapped[uuid.UUID]` annotation with `mapped_column` is the correct SQLAlchemy 2.0 pattern for mixins, but it only works when the concrete model class also inherits from `Base` (`DeclarativeBase` subclass). As written this is correct in intent and consistent with SQLAlchemy mixin docs, so this is not a bug per se — but the class has no docstring note and no explicit inheritance from anything. SQLAlchemy mixin classes that use `mapped_column` without inheriting `MappedAsDataclass` or `Base` can be confusing and are sensitive to ordering in multiple-inheritance declarations (`class Foo(UUIDPKMixin, Base)` works; `class Foo(Base, UUIDPKMixin)` may not depending on SA version). A brief usage note in the docstring ("Must appear before `Base` in the MRO") would prevent downstream errors. This is a documentation gap, not a code defect.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`base.py:98` — `values_callable` lambda parameter name shadows the outer parameter**

`values_callable=lambda cls: [member.value for member in cls]` — the lambda parameter `cls` shadows the outer function's `enum_cls` name. This creates no runtime error (the lambda is called by SQLAlchemy with the enum class as argument, not the outer `enum_cls`), and the logic is correct. Renaming the lambda parameter to `e` or `members` would improve clarity: `lambda e: [m.value for m in e]`.

**`base.py:75` — `Uuid` type vs `UUID` type**

SQLAlchemy provides both `sqlalchemy.Uuid` (added in 2.0) and the older `sqlalchemy.dialects.postgresql.UUID`. Using `sqlalchemy.Uuid` is correct for the declared Python 3.11+ / SA 2.0 baseline. No action needed — this is just a confirmation that the choice is intentional and modern.

**`enums.py` — no `__all__`**

`models/enums.py` does not define `__all__`. While the public API is controlled by `models/__init__.py.__all__`, adding `__all__` to `enums.py` is consistent with the project's re-export conventions and makes the module self-documenting. Minor omission given the re-export layer handles it.

### Assessment

**Task quality:** Approved

**Reasoning:** Every interface specified in the brief is implemented correctly, the critical `str_enum` correctness properties (`native_enum=False`, value-not-name storage) are verified by tests that pass, all global constraints (type hints, `from __future__ import annotations`, Google docstrings, `StrEnum`, UTC-aware timestamps) are satisfied, and TDD evidence is complete. The only findings are a documentation gap on mixin MRO ordering and a cosmetic lambda parameter name — neither blocks downstream tasks.</result>

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)
None.

#### Important (Should Fix)
None.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**tool.py:67-69 — `server_default` missing for DB-level defaults**

`gpu_count` and `enabled` use SQLAlchemy's `default=` (Python-side only), not `server_default=`. This means a row inserted via raw SQL or another ORM session without touching these columns will get `NULL` rather than `1`/`true` at the database level. For a catalog table likely to be seeded or synced from external scripts, a `server_default` of `"1"` / `"true"` would make the schema self-enforcing. The current approach is acceptable for pure-ORM access (which is the stated use case for this task), so this is polish, not a defect.

**test_tool.py:119 — `count == 2` is session-contamination-sensitive**

The assertion `count == 2` assumes a clean database state with no pre-existing `Tool` rows from other tests. If test isolation ever weakens (e.g., a session-scoped fixture is introduced), this test will spuriously fail. A more robust pattern would be `assert count &gt;= 2` or use a dedicated query filtered by `name == "boltz"`. Not a current defect given integration tests likely use transaction rollback per test, but worth noting for future maintainability.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`artifact.py:81` — `run` relationship missing `lazy="selectin"`**

The relationship `run: Mapped[Run] = relationship(back_populates="artifacts")` uses the default `lazy="select"`, which issues a synchronous lazy load. In an async SQLAlchemy session this raises `sqlalchemy.exc.MissingGreenlet` the moment any code accesses `artifact.run` without an explicit `selectinload`. The test at `test_artifact.py:164` (`assert artifact.run.id == run.id`) accesses this relationship after a `db_session.refresh(artifact)` — if the test fixture uses `expire_on_commit=False` or the session happened to keep the object in its identity map, it can pass by accident without actually exercising a load. Production code that accesses `artifact.run` on a freshly fetched object will fail at runtime.

Fix: add `lazy="selectin"` (matching whatever convention the other models use) or ensure all call sites use `options(selectinload(Artifact.run))`. Whichever pattern the other relationships in this project follow should be applied consistently here.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`test_artifact.py:164` — relationship access without explicit eager load**

Related to the above: the test asserts `artifact.run.id == run.id` after `db_session.refresh(artifact)` but does not pass `attribute_names=["run"]` to `refresh()` or use a `selectinload`. If `lazy="selectin"` is added to the relationship this resolves automatically. If it is not added, the test should load the relationship explicitly (e.g., via `await db_session.refresh(artifact, attribute_names=["run"])` or re-fetching with `options(selectinload(Artifact.run))`).

The one issue (`lazy="select"` on an async relationship) is a latent runtime bug that did not prevent the test suite from passing but will surface in production; it should be addressed before this model is used in application code, but it does not block merging if the project has a consistent async query pattern that always uses explicit `selectinload`.</result>

---

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`system.py:19` — `maintenance_mode` SQLAlchemy-side `default` is not a `server_default`**

`maintenance_mode: Mapped[bool] = mapped_column(Boolean, default=False, nullable=False)`

The `default=False` is a Python/ORM-side default. It works for ORM-constructed objects, but if a row is ever inserted via raw SQL (migrations, fixtures, manual psql) it will `NULL` if the column has no `server_default`. The brief's code is identical here — this is not a deviation from spec — but it is a latent schema hazard. The safe fix is to add `server_default=false()` (importing `false` from `sqlalchemy`) alongside the ORM `default`:

```python
from sqlalchemy import Boolean, CheckConstraint, DateTime, Integer, false, func

maintenance_mode: Mapped[bool] = mapped_column(
    Boolean, default=False, server_default=false(), nullable=False
)
```

This is a should-fix, not critical, because all current insert paths go through the ORM.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`access.py:77` — `email` index is redundant given the unique constraint**

`email: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(String(320), unique=True, index=True, nullable=False)`

`unique=True` already causes SQLAlchemy/Postgres to create a unique index; `index=True` generates a second, non-unique index on the same column. This wastes space and write overhead. The `index=True` argument should be removed. Again, this matches the brief verbatim — not an implementer error — but it is a schema cleanness issue worth flagging.

## Review: Plan 2 (Data Model &amp; Migrations) — `feature/data-model` (668431f..303468d)

### Strengths

- **Clean plan correction.** The `cc11d38` mid-execution fix (defer relationships until both endpoint models exist) is technically correct: SQLAlchemy resolves `relationship()` targets at mapper-configuration time, and `User.runs -&gt; Run` before `Run` is mapped raises `InvalidRequestError`. The corrected sequencing (User/Tool relationship-free in Tasks 2/3; `Run` + `User.runs`/`Tool.runs` wired in Task 4; `Run.artifacts` + `Artifact.run` in Task 5) is the standard idiom and matches the final committed files exactly.
- **Constraint-naming convention** (`base.py:8-14` of the diff / `NAMING_CONVENTION`) is correctly applied and flows through to the migration: `pk_users`, `uq_users_email`, `fk_runs_user_id_users`, `ck_system_settings_single_row`, etc. This is exactly what makes future Alembic autogenerate stable.
- **`str_enum` helper** (`base.py`) is the right call: `native_enum=False` + `values_callable` stores enum *values* (`"admin"`, not `"ADMIN"`), `length` auto-sized. Confirmed round-tripping by `test_user_role_round_trips_as_value`. This makes enum evolution a data migration, not a Postgres `ALTER TYPE` dance.
- **Migration covers all eight tables** (`migrations/versions/4ae9f1f0e12e_initial_schema.py`): `system_settings`, `tools`, `users`, `allowed_emails`, `audit_logs`, `password_reset_tokens`, `runs`, `artifacts`, with `downgrade()` dropping them in reverse FK order. The `01cc70c` honesty fix (`refresh(artifact, attribute_names=["run"])` in `test_artifact.py`) genuinely forces a relationship load instead of reading an identity-map cache hit — good catch by per-task review.
- **No-drift test is real** (`tests/test_migrations.py`): `command.upgrade(head)` then `command.check()` against the migrated DB; `AutogenerateDiffsDetected` fails the test. This catches model/migration divergence in CI.
- **Carry-forwards are correct.** `dispose_engine()` (`db.py`) is idempotent and clears both singletons; `lifespan` (`main.py`) disposes on shutdown; the auto-skip hook (`tests/conftest.py`) works both directions. Marker is registered in `pyproject.toml`, `asyncio_mode = "auto"`, sequential runner (no xdist) — so the shared-DB tests don't collide.

### Minor-findings triage

- **[P2T1] UUIDPKMixin MRO docstring note** — defer-to-nice-to-have. Usage is correct everywhere (`class User(UUIDPKMixin, TimestampMixin, Base)`); purely a doc nicety.
- **[P2T1] `str_enum` lambda param `cls` shadows `enum_cls`** — defer (cosmetic). The lambda receives SQLAlchemy's enum class at call time; functionally correct, only a readability nit.
- **[P2T1] `enums.py` no `__all__`** — defer (cosmetic). Public API is the re-export layer in `models/__init__.py`, which has `__all__`.
- **[P2T3] Python-side `default=` vs `server_default`** — resolved already by `8ebd468`, which added `server_default` to `gpu_count`/`enabled`/`maintenance_mode`. Remaining Python-only defaults are the enum columns (`role`/`tier`/`status`/`status`) — see Important #1 below.
- **[P2T3] `test_tool` count==2 relies on fresh-schema isolation** — defer. Guaranteed by `db_session` drop/create; acceptable.
- **[P2T4] `__init__.py` alphabetical import order** — defer/no-action. Correct call; SQLAlchemy defers resolution, and dependency-ordering would fight isort.
- **[P2T5 → PLAN 5 decision] relationship loading strategy** — **defer-to-Plan-5, sound** (expanded below).
- **[P2T7] `gpu_count` `server_default="1"` bare-string vs `sa.text("1")`** — defer (stylistic; both valid DDL).
- **[P2T8] probe catches `(SQLAlchemyError, OSError)`** — defer/no-action. Justified: asyncpg surfaces `ConnectionRefusedError` (an `OSError`) unwrapped; rule-compliant (specific, not bare).
- **[P2T8] skip-reason wording differs from brief** — defer (immaterial).

**On the Plan-5 deferral specifically:** Deferring is sound, and nothing must change in the models now. With default `lazy="select"`, touching an unloaded relationship on a cold (e.g. just-`refresh`ed without the attribute, or detached) object in async raises `MissingGreenlet` — but that is a *query-site* concern, correctly owned by the service layer. The ledger's loader guidance is also correct and worth preserving for Plan 5: use `selectinload` for the to-many collections (`User.runs`, `Tool.runs`, `Run.artifacts`) and `joinedload`/`selectinload` for the many-to-one scalars (`Run.user`, `Run.tool`, `Artifact.run`) — note the ledger's phrasing ("selectin is WRONG for the one-to-many collections") is backwards; `selectinload` is in fact the *preferred* strategy for collections. I'd flag that wording so Plan 5 doesn't act on it inverted. The one thing I'd *recommend* (not require) for Plan 5: add `lazy="raise_on_sql"` as a guardrail so a forgotten eager-load fails loudly at dev time instead of emitting an implicit lazy load. Not a model change needed now.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)
None.

#### Important (Should Fix)
1. **Enum columns have no `server_default`; non-enum defaulted columns do** — `user.py` (`role`/`tier`/`status`), `run.py` (`status`). `8ebd468` added `server_default` to `gpu_count`, `enabled`, `maintenance_mode`, but the enum-backed columns still rely on Python-side `default=` only. This is an inconsistency that bites the moment a row is inserted outside the ORM (raw SQL seed, a future bulk `INSERT`, or a data migration): `users.role`/`tier`/`status` and `runs.status` are `NOT NULL` with no DB default and would reject the insert, whereas `gpu_count`/`enabled` would not. Either add `server_default=&lt;value&gt;` to all four enum columns (e.g. `server_default="user"`, `"standard"`, `"pending"`, `"queued"`) for consistency, or consciously decide enum defaults are ORM-only and document it. Given `8ebd468`'s stated intent ("add server_default to defaulted columns"), the enum columns appear to have been missed. *Note: this is a model+migration change; doing it now keeps the migration regeneration in this plan rather than spawning a churn migration in Plan 3.*

#### Minor (Nice to Have)
1. **Composite `UniqueConstraint("name", "version")` names as `uq_tools_name`** (migration line `uq_tools_name`). The convention uses `%(column_0_name)s`, so the constraint name references only the first column. It's unique within the table and works, but a reader scanning constraints sees `uq_tools_name` for what is really a `(name, version)` uniqueness — mildly misleading. Acceptable to leave (changing the convention to include both columns risks identifier-length issues elsewhere); worth a one-line comment if you care.
2. **`ix_runs_user_id_hidden_at` is hand-named, bypassing the convention** (`run.py` `__table_args__`). The convention would have produced `ix_runs_user_id` for an `Index(None, ...)` — but since a *separate* `ix_runs_user_id` already exists (from `user_id`'s `index=True`), the explicit name is actually necessary to avoid collision. Correct as-is; flagging only because it's the one constraint not following the auto-convention, which a future reader might "fix" and break.
3. **`runs.user_id` has both a single-column index (`ix_runs_user_id`) and is the lead column of the composite `ix_runs_user_id_hidden_at`.** The composite can serve `user_id`-only lookups, so `ix_runs_user_id` is arguably redundant. Negligible cost at this scale; revisit only if write volume on `runs` becomes high. No action now.

### Recommendations
- **Plan 5 (service layer):** adopt explicit eager loading at query sites (`selectinload` for collections, `joinedload`/`selectinload` for scalars). Correct the inverted note in the ledger before designing queries. Consider `lazy="raise_on_sql"` as a dev guardrail.
- **Process:** the per-task `server_default` cleanup (`8ebd468`) is exactly the kind of cross-cutting hygiene pass that should sweep *all* defaulted columns in one go — the enum columns slipping through is why Important #1 exists. A quick "grep for `default=` without `server_default=`" check would have caught it.
- **`audit_logs` growth:** as an append-only, time-series-ish table, it has `ix_audit_logs_created_at` already (good for time-window queries). When Plan 4+ adds admin filtering by `(actor_id, created_at)` or `(action, created_at)`, consider composite indexes then — no action now.

### Assessment
**Ready to merge?** With fixes.
**Reasoning:** The data model, migration, and tests are well-structured, the relationship-deferral correction is sound, and all eight entities plus carry-forwards are present and genuinely exercised against real Postgres. The one substantive item is the missing `server_default` on the four enum columns (Important #1) — an inconsistency best resolved now while the initial migration is still being regenerated rather than via a churn migration later; everything else is defer-able cosmetic or correctly owned by Plan 5.</result>

The brief's own example code for `__init__.py` omits it, which is why the implementer missed it. However, the global constraint is explicit, and consistency matters for a growing package. Technically harmless today since there are no type annotations in the file, but it's a stated non-negotiable.

### Strengths

- `get_current_user` correctly handles every failure mode in sequence: missing key → 401, malformed UUID → 401, user not found → 401, user not ACTIVE → 401. The guard `user.status is not UserStatus.ACTIVE` uses identity comparison against the enum, which is correct for SQLAlchemy-mapped `StrEnum`/`Enum` columns.
- `login` correctly orders checks: authenticate first (bad credentials → 401 before status is checked), then status (pending → 403 "pending approval", otherwise → 403 "disabled"). Session is set only after both guards pass. This ordering is important — it avoids leaking whether an email exists based on status codes for wrong-password attempts.
- `_UNAUTHENTICATED` as a module-level singleton avoids per-request object allocation and is fine here because FastAPI does not mutate `HTTPException` instances after they are raised.
- `UserRead` declares only `id`, `email`, `display_name`, `role`, `tier`, `status` — `hashed_password` is absent. `from_attributes=True` is set via `ConfigDict`, so returning the ORM `User` object from endpoint functions is safe.
- `logout` calls `request.session.clear()`, not `del request.session["user_id"]`, so any other stale session keys are also removed.
- `register` maps `RegistrationNotAllowed` → 403 and `EmailAlreadyRegistered` → 409 with `str(exc)` as the detail and chains the original exception with `from exc`.
- Tests are exactly what the brief specifies and cover all named scenarios end-to-end against real Postgres.
- `from __future__ import annotations` is present in every new module including `schemas/__init__.py`.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`src/fold_at_scripps/auth/dependencies.py:13-14` — Mutable singleton `HTTPException` is safe today but fragile by contract.**

`_UNAUTHENTICATED` is constructed once at import time. FastAPI and Starlette do not mutate `HTTPException` instances, so this is currently safe. However, if a future middleware or exception handler ever adds instance attributes (e.g., attaching request context), sharing the singleton across requests would cause a race condition. The conventional pattern is either a factory function or raising inline. This is a low-probability risk given the codebase, but worth noting for the next developer.

How to fix: Convert to a factory or raise inline in each branch. Given the three raise sites are all in one function, inline is cleaner:

```python
raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="Not authenticated")
```

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`tests/api/test_auth.py:272-273` — `_client()` creates a new `create_app()` on every call.**

`create_app()` is called inside `_client()` with no arguments, which means each test that calls `_client()` builds a fresh app including re-registering middleware. This is intentional (and matches the brief verbatim), but it means each test creates an isolated session store — so the cookie from one `_client()` context cannot carry over to a different one. This is fine for the current tests since each test opens exactly one `async with _client()` block, but if a future test needs to share cookies across two `_client()` scopes it will silently fail. Not a correctness issue in the current suite.

**`src/fold_at_scripps/schemas/auth.py:37` — `UserRead.email` typed as `str` instead of `EmailStr`.**

The `email` field on `UserRead` is `str`, while `RegisterRequest.email` and `LoginRequest.email` are `EmailStr`. This is not a bug — the stored email is already validated at registration time — but using `EmailStr` in `UserRead` would make the output schema self-documenting in the OpenAPI spec. Purely cosmetic.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None. The implementation is functionally correct and fully spec-compliant.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`_run_async()` in production `cli.py` — concern 1** (`src/fold_at_scripps/cli.py:70–88`)

The helper exists solely because `typer.testing.CliRunner.invoke` is synchronous but is called from inside an `async def` test function running under pytest-asyncio's event loop. The production code path (no running loop) takes the `else` branch and calls `asyncio.run` directly — zero behavioral difference. The thread-executor branch is only reachable when the caller already has a loop running, which never happens in production.

The proper fix is test-side: wrap `runner.invoke(...)` in `asyncio.to_thread(runner.invoke, app, args)` inside the test, or make the test functions sync (the `db_session` fixture query is the only async operation; it could be replaced by a direct database check using `psycopg2` or by structuring the test differently). However, the spec itself mandated `async def` test functions that mix `CliRunner.invoke` with `await db_session.scalar(...)` — there is no clean sync alternative given that constraint. The implementer chose the minimal invasive fix.

The real concern is conceptual purity: production code is carrying a guard clause whose only purpose is to handle a test harness limitation. This is a code smell. But in this specific case, the guard is inert in production, the helper is private (underscore-prefixed), it's 18 lines, and removing it would require restructuring the tests beyond the scope of this task. It is a reasonable engineering trade-off for a one-shot bootstrap CLI, not a hot path.

**Verdict:** Should fix in a follow-up by restructuring `test_cli.py` to use `asyncio.to_thread` (making the tests `async def` with `await asyncio.to_thread(runner.invoke, ...)`) and removing `_run_async` from `cli.py`. Not a blocker for this task.

**asyncpg `RuntimeWarning` during test teardown — concern 3** (`tests/test_cli.py`, teardown path via `_run_async`)

The global constraint says test output should be pristine. The implementer acknowledges this warning is emitted and attributes it to asyncpg internals when connections are closed from a thread. This is a real finding: warnings are findings per the stated standard, not acceptable noise. The warning is triggered by the thread-pool path in `_run_async`, which is itself a test-only artifact.

If `_run_async` is removed (see above) and the tests call `runner.invoke` via `asyncio.to_thread`, the thread-pool-based teardown issue disappears because asyncpg cleanup happens normally within the main loop. This is the correct fix and it resolves both concern 1 and concern 3 together.

**Verdict:** Impure test output is a should-fix, and the root cause is the same as concern 1. Fix both together.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`@app.callback()` with no-op body — concern 2** (`src/fold_at_scripps/cli.py:91–93`)

This is idiomatic Typer for forcing group/multi-command mode when only one command is registered. Typer's own documentation recommends this pattern. The callback body is empty (only a docstring), the command names are unchanged, and public UX is identical. This is not a smell — it is the correct, minimal workaround for a Typer 0.12+ behavior change. No fix needed; the note is informational only.

**`typer` as a production dependency, not a dev dependency**

The console script `fold-admin` is installed as a production entry point, so `typer` correctly belongs in `[project] dependencies`. No issue here.

## Review Complete

### Strengths

- **Clean architecture / boundaries.** Domain logic is genuinely transport-agnostic: `auth/passwords.py`, `auth/providers.py` (`IdentityProvider` Protocol + `LocalIdentityProvider`), and `auth/service.py` carry no FastAPI imports. The router (`api/auth.py`) is a thin shell that maps domain exceptions to HTTP codes. Adding SSO/LDAP later is genuinely additive — swap `get_identity_provider()` (`providers.py:39`) to return a different `IdentityProvider`; registration being local-specific lives separately in `service.py`, so it won't get dragged along.
- **Per-request status enforcement is correct and is the security crux.** `get_current_user` (`auth/dependencies.py`) re-loads the user via `session.get(User, user_id)` and rejects unless `status is UserStatus.ACTIVE` on every request. Disabling a user takes effect immediately — the cookie carries only `user_id`, never status. This matches the plan's central design claim.
- **No credential leakage.** `UserRead` (`schemas/auth.py`) is an explicit allowlist of fields and omits `hashed_password`; `/login`, `/me`, `/register` all go through `response_model=UserRead`, so the hash cannot escape even though endpoints return ORM `User` objects.
- **Login enumeration handled where it matters.** Both unknown-email and wrong-password return the same generic 401 "Invalid email or password" (`api/auth.py`), and the provider returns `None` for both — no message-based oracle on the credential path.
- **Defense in depth on the duplicate-email check.** Service pre-checks (`service.py`), and the `User.email` column is `unique=True` (`models/user.py`) — DB constraint backs the application check.
- **CLI is now one-shot safe.** The `dca6ba6` refactor wraps the work in `try/finally: await dispose_engine()`, and `dispose_engine` (`db.py`) nulls both `_engine` and `_sessionmaker` — idempotent and clean. Duplicate email exits non-zero via `typer.Exit(code=1)`. The prior test-only thread helper was removed; tests now drive the CLI with `asyncio.to_thread(runner.invoke, ...)` (`tests/test_cli.py`), keeping the event loop unblocked.
- **Tests exercise real rejection paths against real Postgres** with a cookie-carrying `AsyncClient`: pending→403, wrong-password→401, unauthenticated `/me`→401, and a full login→me→logout→401 round-trip proving the session cookie is set and cleared.

### Findings triage

- **[P3T1] docstring-only `__init__.py` lacking `from __future__ import annotations`** → **defer (exempt docstring-only files).** A `from __future__` import in a file with zero annotations is pure ceremony. Note the framing is slightly off: `schemas/__init__.py` already has the import (diff line 466), and the root `src/fold_at_scripps/__init__.py` is *not* docstring-only (it has `__version__ = "0.1.0"`) yet correctly needs no future-import. The only genuinely-bare file is `auth/__init__.py`. Recommend codifying "docstring-only `__init__.py` is exempt" rather than a sweep. Not merge-blocking.
- **[P3T5] module-level `_UNAUTHENTICATED` HTTPException singleton** → **defer (or trivially inline now).** Confirmed not a current defect — Starlette raises it, reads `.status_code`/`.detail`, never mutates it, and re-raising the same instance is fine. The latent risk (future code mutating a shared exception) is real but tiny. If touched again, inline the three raises; otherwise leave it. Not merge-blocking.
- **[P3T5] `UserRead.email` typed `str` while requests use `EmailStr`** → **defer.** Cosmetic; output-only self-documentation. Stored emails already passed `EmailStr` validation at registration, so output validation adds nothing. Optionally tighten to `EmailStr` for symmetry.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)
None. No auth-bypass or credential-leak path found. Pending/disabled users cannot obtain a session (login 403s before `request.session["user_id"]` is set), and a forged cookie fails signature verification at `SessionMiddleware`; even a validly-signed cookie for a since-disabled/deleted user is rejected per-request by `get_current_user`.

#### Important (Should Fix)
None that block this lightweight intranet merge. The items below are deliberately Minor given the stated threat model.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

1. **Timing oracle for user enumeration — `auth/providers.py:30-36`.** When the email is unknown, `authenticate` returns immediately without calling `verify_password`, so an unknown email responds measurably faster than a known one (which pays the full Argon2 cost). This leaks account existence via timing, partially undercutting the generic 401 message. *Why it matters (proportionately): low — registration is allowlist-gated and this is intranet attribution, not hardened security.* *Fix if desired:* verify against a fixed dummy hash on the `user is None` branch (compute one module-level `_DUMMY_HASH = hash_password("…")` and call `verify_password(password, _DUMMY_HASH)` before returning `None`).

2. **Distinct 403 detail strings reveal account state — `api/auth.py` (login).** "Account is pending approval" vs "Account is disabled" confirms a known account and discloses its lifecycle state to an unauthenticated caller. This is a reasonable UX tradeoff (a pending user *should* be told to wait), so flagging only for awareness — likely keep as-is.

3. **Dev-default `secret_key` is overridable but silent — `config.py:18`.** `secret_key = "dev-insecure-secret-change-me"` is correctly overridable via `FOLD_SECRET_KEY` and `session_https_only` via `FOLD_SESSION_HTTPS_ONLY`. There is no startup guard warning if the insecure default is still in use in a non-debug/production context. Not in this plan's scope, but worth a one-line check later (e.g., refuse to boot with the default when `debug is False`). The `same_site="lax"` choice is correct for a cookie-session app.

### Recommendations

- **Process:** the progress-ledger framing of finding [P3T1] should be corrected before it propagates — two of the three named files don't actually need the change (one already has it; one has a module statement). Confirm the "exempt docstring-only `__init__.py`" rule in the global conventions so future plans don't re-litigate it.
- **For Plan 8 (admin console):** when `activate`/`disable` endpoints land, add a test that an *already-authenticated* user is locked out on their next request after being disabled (the mechanism exists in `get_current_user`; lock it in with a test). Also consider the `_DUMMY_HASH` timing fix then, alongside `require_admin`.
- **Optional hardening (any later plan):** add the startup secret-key guard noted above; it's cheap insurance against shipping the dev secret.

### Assessment

**Ready to merge?** Yes.

**Reasoning:** The auth flow is correct end-to-end with no bypass or credential-leak path — pending/disabled users can't get a session, status is re-checked per request, and `hashed_password` never escapes `UserRead`. All three logged minors are correctly defer-able (and one is partly mischaracterized in the ledger); the new findings (timing oracle, state-revealing 403s, silent dev secret) are genuinely minor under the stated intranet/attribution threat model and don't gate this merge.</result>

- Auth guard is correct on both endpoints: `_: User = Depends(get_current_user)` appears in both `list_tools` and `get_tool` signatures — unauthenticated requests will receive 401 as confirmed by the passing test.
- `enabled.is_(True)` in `list_enabled_tools` (service.py:96) is the correct SQLAlchemy idiom for boolean comparison — avoids the `== True` pitfall that generates ambiguous SQL on some dialects.
- `get_enabled_tool` uses `session.get()` (primary key lookup, identity-map aware) rather than a full `select`, then checks `tool.enabled` in Python — correct and efficient for single-object retrieval.
- `ToolSummary` deliberately excludes `input_schema` (list response is lighter), `ToolRead` includes it — split is clean and matches the brief.
- `ConfigDict(from_attributes=True)` on `ToolSummary` (inherited by `ToolRead`) enables ORM → Pydantic serialization without triggering relationship traversal, as long as `ToolSummary`/`ToolRead` reference only scalar columns (they do — no relationship fields are declared).
- Results ordered by name in `list_enabled_tools` — deterministic ordering that makes the category-filter test's list-equality assertion reliable.
- Tests cover all five scenarios called out in the review checklist: unauth-401, enabled-list, category filter, disabled-excluded + detail-404, detail-includes-schema.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`get_tool` missing return type annotation** — `api/tools.py:49`

```python
@router.get("/{tool_id}", response_model=ToolRead)
async def get_tool(
    tool_id: uuid.UUID,
    session: AsyncSession = Depends(get_session),
    _: User = Depends(get_current_user),
):
```

The function has no `-&gt; ...` return annotation. The global constraint requires type hints on all function signatures. `list_tools` has `-&gt; list` (which is acceptable if not maximally precise). `get_tool` has nothing. Should be `-&gt; ToolRead` (or `-&gt; Tool` to match what the service returns, with FastAPI handling the conversion via `response_model`). `-&gt; ToolRead` is the most honest declaration here since FastAPI will serialize it that way.

Fix: add `-&gt; ToolRead` to the signature at `api/tools.py:54`.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`list_tools` return type is `-&gt; list` (unparameterized)** — `api/tools.py:44`

The return annotation is `-&gt; list` rather than `-&gt; list[Tool]` or `-&gt; list[ToolSummary]`. This is weakly typed and inconsistent with the project standard of precise type hints. The service returns `list[Tool]`; the endpoint converts via `response_model`. Annotating as `-&gt; list[Tool]` is most accurate. Not a correctness issue — FastAPI ignores the Python return annotation in favor of `response_model` — but it creates a misleading signal for static analysis.

Fix: change `-&gt; list` to `-&gt; list[Tool]` (and add `Tool` to the import from `fold_at_scripps.models`, which is already imported) at `api/tools.py:44`.

Here is my whole-branch review of `feature/tool-catalog` (ebfaf03..8941eae).

---

### Strengths

- **Clean source boundary.** `catalog/sources.py:18` (`ToolSource` Protocol) + `FakeToolSource` cleanly decouples sync/read/API from autobio. Only the thin `autobio_source.py` touches `subprocess`, and the real-CLI tests are guarded with `@pytest.mark.skipif(shutil.which("autobio") is None, ...)` (`tests/catalog/test_autobio_source.py:62`, `tests/test_cli.py:58`), so CI stays green without autobio. This is exactly the architecture the plan called for.
- **Subprocess usage is textbook-safe.** `autobio_source.py:_run_json` uses list args (no `shell=True`), `check=True`, explicit `timeout`, `capture_output=True`, `text=True`. Matches the global instruction against `shell=True`.
- **Sync semantics are correct.** `service.py:_apply` deliberately omits `enabled`; new tools created `enabled=True` (`service.py:243`); single `await session.commit()` at the end makes the run atomic. The `test_sync_preserves_enabled_flag` test genuinely exercises the admin-flag-preservation path against real Postgres.
- **No lazy-load on serialization.** `db.py:get_sessionmaker` sets `expire_on_commit=False`, and `ToolSummary`/`ToolRead` (`schemas/tools.py`) declare only scalar fields — the `runs` relationship is never touched during response serialization. `list_enabled_tools` returns a materialized `list(...)`. No N+1 on the read path.
- **Read API is properly gated.** Both endpoints depend on `get_current_user` (which returns 401 when unauthenticated, `auth/dependencies.py:21`); `get_enabled_tool` returns `None` for disabled tools → 404, so disabled tools leak via neither list nor detail (`test_disabled_tool_excluded` covers both).
- **Migration is incremental and drift-clean.** `8e1814737b0a` adds exactly the four columns and chains correctly off `8134eced0fe3` (verified linear head, single revision). `supports_batch` carries `server_default=sa.text("false")` matching the model's `server_default=false()`.
- **`from_attributes` / `ToolSummary` vs `ToolRead` split is exactly per spec** — summary excludes `input_schema`/`image_tag`/`default_timeout`; `ToolRead` adds them via inheritance.

### Findings triage

- **(a) `AutobioToolSource.fetch_tools` is N+1 subprocess calls** — **defer (to a future perf pass; not a plan task).** By design and acceptable: ~7s for ~50 tools on an infrequent admin-only sync. The plan's "Out of scope" + the ledger both acknowledge this. No fix needed before merge.
- **(b) `_sync_catalog` private helper missing a docstring** — **defer-to-final-sweep (or fix now, trivial).** Project rule is public-only docstrings, so this is optional. Note the sibling `_create_admin` is also a private helper; check whether *it* has one for consistency. Not a merge blocker.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)
None.

#### Important (Should Fix)
None.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

- **`api/tools.py:35` — `get_tool` returns the ORM `Tool` but is annotated `-&gt; ToolRead`.** The function returns `tool` (a `Tool` ORM instance), and FastAPI coerces it via `response_model=ToolRead`. The annotation `-&gt; ToolRead` is therefore technically inaccurate (it returns `Tool`, FastAPI does the conversion). Compare `list_tools` which is honestly annotated `-&gt; list[Tool]`. This is purely cosmetic — runtime behavior is correct — but the two endpoints are inconsistent with each other. Consider `-&gt; Tool` on `get_tool` for consistency, or accept the FastAPI idiom. (Commit 7d57351 was specifically about return annotations, so worth a glance.) Not a blocker.

- **`service.py:_apply` docstring** says "(never touches `enabled`)" — good, but the contract that `name`/`version` are also never re-applied (they're the match key, set only at construction) is implicit. Fine as-is; noting for the Plan 8 author who will extend this.

- **Consistency nit (no action):** `gpu_count` is the only `info` field read with `.get(..., 0)` default while peers use strict indexing. Given the verified CLI always returns `gpu_count`, the fallback is slightly inconsistent with the fail-fast treatment of `default_timeout`/`supports_batch`, but it's a harmless safety net.

### Recommendations

- **Plan 8 (admin console):** when adding enable/disable + auto-disable-vanished-tools, the current `_apply`/`sync_catalog` is a clean extension point — add a "seen names" diff after the upsert loop rather than reworking the loop.
- **Plan 6 (executor):** `image_tag`/`default_timeout` are now snapshotted and exposed only via `ToolRead`; confirm the executor reads them from the catalog row (not re-shelling to autobio), per the architecture.
- **Process:** the `(name, version)` upsert key combined with autobio reusing `version: "1.0.0"` across image rebuilds means a rebuilt-but-same-version tool updates in place (input_schema/image_tag refreshed) — correct for v1, but worth flagging to whoever owns autobio versioning so semver bumps actually happen on contract changes.

### Strengths

- The `Storage` Protocol is a clean boundary: method signatures are exactly as specified, which makes the abstraction swappable without touching callers.
- `list_outputs` correctly uses `rglob("*")` with `p.is_file()` guard, so it handles nested subdirectories in outputs without confusing directories for files.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`storage.py:105` — `input_path` does no filename sanitization (path traversal risk)**

`filename` is joined directly onto the inputs directory with no validation:
```python
return self.run_root(run_id) / "inputs" / filename
```
If a caller passes `"../config/config.json"` or `"../../other_run_id/inputs/secret"`, `pathlib` resolves it silently and the returned `Path` escapes the run directory entirely. The brief does not call for validation, but this method exists to handle uploaded files — a context where malicious filenames are a realistic threat. A one-line guard is enough:

```python
def input_path(self, run_id: uuid.UUID, filename: str) -&gt; Path:
    base = self.run_root(run_id) / "inputs"
    resolved = (base / filename).resolve()
    if not resolved.is_relative_to(base.resolve()):
        raise ValueError(f"filename escapes inputs directory: {filename!r}")
    return resolved
```

There is no test covering this vector — the test suite would need a complementary case.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`tests/test_storage.py:163` — `import json` inside function body**

The `json` import inside `test_write_config_round_trips` is a direct copy from the brief. It works and passes ruff, but it violates the project's import ordering convention (stdlib imports belong at module top with isort). Worth hoisting.

**`storage.py:115` — sort order is filesystem-path lexicographic, not documented**

`sorted(p for p in outputs.rglob("*") ...)` sorts by the full absolute path, which is deterministic but not explicitly documented. Because `list_outputs` returns `list[StoredFile]`, callers may rely on the order. A brief docstring note ("sorted by relative path") would lock in the contract.

---

**Task quality:** Approved

**Reasoning:** All specified interfaces are implemented correctly, the directory layout matches the brief, tests exercise the right behaviors with `tmp_path`, and all global style constraints are met. The one flag worth noting before the next task uses `input_path` in production is the unsanitized filename parameter, but it does not break any current spec requirement.</result>

<result>### Spec Compliance

---

### Strengths

- Migration is a clean autogenerated incremental file with correct `down_revision`, `server_default` on both columns, and proper downgrade.

- The `_reset_to_base` docstring accurately explains the problem it solves.

---

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`tests/test_migrations.py` — `_reset_to_base` correctness under the stated failure scenario**

The problem the implementer describes is real: `db_session` uses `create_all`/`drop_all`, which leaves `alembic_version` recording a revision even after tables are physically dropped. The fix — `command.downgrade(config, "base")` before each `upgrade("head")` — is structurally correct: Alembic's `downgrade base` walks the chain of `downgrade()` functions in reverse. If every migration's `downgrade()` uses `op.drop_column` / `op.drop_table` and Postgres silently ignores `IF NOT EXISTS`... wait, it does NOT: `op.drop_column` on a non-existent column raises. So the "alembic_version at head, tables dropped" case would cause `_reset_to_base` itself to fail (executing the head migration's `downgrade()` against tables that don't exist), not silently succeed.

However: the `db_session` fixture uses SQLAlchemy `drop_all` then `create_all`, which drops and recreates ALL tables — including `alembic_version`. So after integration tests that used `db_session`, the `alembic_version` table itself is gone (not stale — absent). A subsequent `upgrade("head")` starting from nothing would succeed fine without `_reset_to_base`.

The real problematic ordering is: migration tests run first (leaving `alembic_version` at `base` after their own downgrade), then `db_session` integration tests run (dropping everything), then a second migration test runs — but the `downgrade` in the prior migration test's `finally` already brought `alembic_version` to `base`. There is no scenario where `alembic_version` says "head" while tables are absent, because `drop_all` removes `alembic_version` too.

This means `_reset_to_base` is defensive but its stated rationale doesn't match actual Postgres + SQLAlchemy behavior. It is not harmful — `downgrade base` from `base` is a no-op, and `downgrade base` from `head` when tables exist works correctly. But the one failure case it claims to handle (`alembic_version = head, tables gone`) would actually cause `downgrade base` to error (drop_column on missing tables), not recover gracefully. The fix works correctly for all realistic orderings, but the claimed edge-case protection is moot.

**Impact on no-drift check:** The no-drift assertion is unweakened. Both `test_migrations_apply_and_match_models` and `test_migration_check_is_clean` call `command.upgrade(config, "head")` after `_reset_to_base`, then call `command.check(config)` against the fully-upgraded live schema. Model-vs-migration drift would still be caught. This is the key property; it holds.

**Recommendation:** The change is safe to merge as-is. Optionally, amend the `_reset_to_base` docstring to more accurately describe its actual benefit ("guards against `alembic_version` being left at an intermediate state by a prior interrupted migration test run") rather than the `create_all`/`drop_all` scenario which doesn't produce the described state.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

- `tests/test_system_settings.py:21` — `test_get_system_settings_creates_singleton` asserts `settings.standard_max_concurrent_runs == 3` but does not assert `power_max_concurrent_runs == 12`. The mirror assertion would be consistent with the defaults test in `test_audit_system.py`. Low priority; the audit test already covers both values.

- `migrations/versions/a787a12a5023_add_quota_settings.py:43,49` — The autogenerate comment `# ### commands auto generated by Alembic - please adjust! ###` / `# ### end Alembic commands ###` is boilerplate noise that could be stripped, but this is convention in many Alembic shops and is not a defect.

---

### Assessment

**Task quality:** Approved

**Reasoning:** All five deliverables match the spec exactly, the migration is incremental with correct server_defaults, the accessor is a correct idempotent singleton, and the no-drift check is not weakened. The `_reset_to_base` addition to `test_migrations.py` is safe (benign in all real orderings) despite its docstring overstating the specific failure scenario it guards against — a docstring clarification is the only meaningful follow-up.</result>

<result>### Spec Compliance

- ✅ `list_runs(session, user) -&gt; list[Run]` implemented, filters `user_id == user.id` and `hidden_at IS NULL`, orders by `created_at DESC`, eager-loads `Run.tool` via `selectinload`.
- ✅ `get_run(session, user, run_id) -&gt; Run | None` implemented, filters by id + ownership + `hidden_at IS NULL`, eager-loads `Run.tool` and `Run.artifacts`, returns `None` via `session.scalar` when no match.

- ✅ `cancel_run(session, user, run_id) -&gt; Run` cancels only QUEUED runs; raises `RunNotCancelable` for non-queued or missing.
- ✅ `soft_delete_run(session, user, run_id) -&gt; Run | None` sets `hidden_at` with timezone-aware UTC timestamp; returns `None` for missing run.
- ✅ Files modified/created match brief exactly: `src/fold_at_scripps/runs/service.py` modified, `tests/runs/test_lifecycle.py` created.

- ✅ `_run` bug fix via `kw.setdefault("status", RunStatus.QUEUED)` is correct — see below.
- ⚠️ The brief's `soft_delete_run` signature says `-&gt; Run | None` but the spec prose says "return it" after deletion (implying `Run`) yet also "None if not found". The implementation returns `Run | None` matching the signature in the brief. This is internally consistent.

**`_run` bug fix verification:** The brief's original helper was `Run(..., status=RunStatus.QUEUED, **kw)`. When `test_cancel_non_queued_raises` calls `_run(..., status=RunStatus.RUNNING)`, `status` appears both as a positional keyword and in `**kw`, causing `TypeError: got multiple values for keyword argument 'status'`. The fix — `kw.setdefault("status", RunStatus.QUEUED)` then `Run(..., **kw)` — correctly ensures `QUEUED` is the default when no `status` is passed, and lets the caller's value win otherwise. This is the minimal correct fix.

---

### Strengths

- Ownership enforcement is airtight: `list_runs` filters `Run.user_id == user.id`; `get_run` filters by id AND `user_id == user.id` AND `hidden_at.is_(None)` in a single SQL WHERE clause, meaning `cancel_run` and `soft_delete_run` (which delegate to `get_run`) cannot operate on another user's run or a hidden run.
- Hidden-run exclusion propagates transitively: `cancel_run` and `soft_delete_run` both call `get_run`, which already enforces `hidden_at IS NULL`, so a previously hidden run cannot be un-hidden via `soft_delete_run` and cannot be cancelled.
- `selectinload` is used in every query touching relationships — no model-level lazy loading changes, consistent with the global constraint.
- `datetime.datetime.now(datetime.UTC)` produces a timezone-aware timestamp, which is correct for `hidden_at`.
- The `is not RunStatus.QUEUED` identity check (rather than `!=`) is appropriate for enum comparison.
- Test coverage directly maps to the spec's concern list: hidden exclusion, other-user exclusion, eager-load verification, ownership on get, cancel queued, cancel non-queued raises, soft-delete hides.

**`tests/runs/test_lifecycle.py:74` — eager-load assertion is optimistic but not definitive.**
`assert runs[0].tool.name == "t"` verifies the attribute is populated and has the right value, which does confirm eager loading worked in practice. However, it does not distinguish between eager-load success and SQLAlchemy resolving the relationship lazily within the same session (lazy-load would still work in test since the session is open). This is a test design limitation inherited from the brief verbatim, not introduced by the implementer. It is not a bug — the `selectinload` is demonstrably in the query at `service.py:62` — but a reviewer looking at the test alone cannot be certain it would catch a regression that removed the `selectinload`. No action needed; just noting it follows the brief.

**`src/fold_at_scripps/runs/service.py:88-95` — `soft_delete_run` returns the mutated `Run` but the return type annotation says `Run | None`.**
The brief signature and prose both specify `Run | None`, and the implementation is consistent with that. However, the function always returns `Run` after finding it (never `None` after the guard). This is completely correct behavior; the `| None` covers the not-found path. No change needed.

## Senior Code Reviewer — Whole-Branch Review: Plan 5 (Service Layer, Storage &amp; Run Lifecycle)

**Range:** f0f0ff8..89c6fcc (9 commits) · **Verification:** `ruff check` clean, `ruff format --check` clean (79 files), `pytest` 86 passed against live Postgres.

### Strengths

- **Clean boundary design.** `Storage` (`storage.py:24`) and `Executor` (`executor.py:30`) are `Protocol`s with `LocalStorage`/`FakeExecutor` as concrete impls. `execute_run` (`runs/service.py:96`) depends only on the protocols, so Plan 6's real autobio executor and Plan 7's HTTP layer drop in without touching this code. The seams are genuinely transport-agnostic — no FastAPI import anywhere in `src/fold_at_scripps/runs/` or `storage.py`/`executor.py`.
- **Quota correctly DB-backed, not env.** `effective_concurrency_limit` (`runs/quota.py:31`) honors per-user override → tier default → `SystemSettings`, exactly per the "operational config lives in the DB, admin-editable later" constraint. The `&gt;=` boundary (`quota.py:44`) and `_IN_FLIGHT = (QUEUED, RUNNING)` (`quota.py:13`) match the plan.
- **Submit ordering is correct and tested.** `submit_run` (`runs/service.py:18`) validates params and checks quota *before* `session.add(run)`, and the tests assert no row/file is created on rejection (`test_submit.py:911`, `:926`) — this is the rollback guarantee the plan calls for, and it's verified, not assumed.
- **Ownership + hidden filtering is airtight.** Every read path filters `Run.user_id == user.id` AND `Run.hidden_at.is_(None)` (`service.py:60`, `:70`), and `cancel_run`/`soft_delete_run` route through `get_run`, so cross-user access is structurally impossible. Tests cover the cross-user negative case (`test_lifecycle.py:743`).
- **Executor runs off the event loop.** `asyncio.to_thread(executor.execute, request)` (`service.py:115`) — correct for a sync, GPU-bound executor; the loop stays responsive. Timing is captured on both success and failure; artifacts indexed only on success (`service.py:120-127`), and the failure path asserts zero artifacts (`test_execute.py:675`).
- **Path-traversal guard is correct.** `input_path` resolves and checks `is_relative_to(base)` (`storage.py:50`), with both positive and negative tests (`test_storage.py:1071`, `:1079`). Good defense ahead of Plan 7 uploads.
- **`selectinload` used explicitly** (`service.py:61,71`) per the relationship-loading constraint; models keep default lazy loading.

### Findings triage

- **[P5T3] `_reset_to_base` migration guard** — **defer-to-Plan-6** (test-infra hardening). Verified adequate for normal operation: every migration test's `finally` runs `downgrade base`, which clears `alembic_version`; the db_session fixture drops its own tables. I exercised the two realistic cross-file orderings (db_session→migration, and migration→db_session→migration) and both pass. The guard only fails to cover an *abnormal* exit (crash/SIGKILL mid-migration-test leaving `alembic_version` at head with tables gone), in which case `downgrade base` would hit a missing-table DROP and fail loudly — never masking drift. That's an acceptable worst case. The docstring is slightly overstated (says "intermediate revision"; the actual stale state is `alembic_version` at *head*), but harmless. Recommend the more robust reset (drop all tables + `alembic_version` unconditionally) only if flakiness ever surfaces — not a merge blocker.
- **[P5T3] `test_get_system_settings_creates_singleton` doesn't assert `power_max==12`** — **defer / won't-fix**. Cosmetic; covered by `test_audit_system.py:605`.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)
None.

#### Important (Should Fix)
None that block this plan. Two contract notes for downstream plans are in Recommendations (TOCTOU quota; `execute_run` state guard) — both are legitimately out of scope for the transport-agnostic core, but Plans 6/7 must handle them.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)
- **`execute_run` doesn't validate input state** — `runs/service.py:104`. It unconditionally sets `RUNNING` regardless of `run.status`. Per the docstring it's meant for a *queued* run, but nothing enforces it; a canceled-then-dispatched run would be resurrected. *Why it matters:* Plan 6's scheduler is the intended caller and owns dispatch, so this is defensible as-is — but a one-line `if run.status is not RunStatus.QUEUED: raise ...` guard would make the seam safer and self-documenting. *Fix:* add the guard, or document in the docstring that the caller guarantees QUEUED. Defer to Plan 6 if the scheduler will enforce it.
- **`output_dir` stores an absolute host path** — `runs/service.py:32` (`run.output_dir = str(storage.run_root(run.id))`). When Storage becomes object storage (per the plan's stated future), an absolute local FS path is meaningless and ties a DB column to the current backend. *Fix:* consider storing a storage-relative key (e.g. `runs/&lt;id&gt;`) and let `Storage` resolve it. Low priority; defer to whenever object storage lands.
- **`cancel_run` conflates not-found with not-cancelable** — `runs/service.py:78`. Both raise `RunNotCancelable`. *Why it matters:* Plan 7 will want 404 vs 409 distinction. *Fix:* let Plan 7's endpoint layer disambiguate (it can call `get_run` first), or split the exceptions later. Defer to Plan 7.

### Recommendations

- **Plan 7 (HTTP API): quota is TOCTOU, not atomic.** `check_quota` counts then `submit_run` inserts with no row lock or DB constraint. Two concurrent submissions by the same user can both pass `&gt;=` and both insert, exceeding the cap. Acceptable for the single-session service core, but Plan 7 (concurrent requests) should add a `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` on the user row, a serializable transaction, or a partial unique/exclusion constraint. Flagging now so it isn't discovered under load.
- **Plan 6 (scheduler): define the `execute_run` failure contract.** Currently an *executor exception* (vs a clean `ExecutionResult(succeeded=False)`) propagates out of `execute_run` and would leave the run stuck in `RUNNING` (status set + committed at line 104 before `to_thread`). The scheduler will need a try/finally to mark such runs FAILED. The signature `(session, run, executor, storage) -&gt; Run` is otherwise right for the scheduler to drive after it sets `assigned_gpu_ids`.
- **Process:** the two accumulated minor findings were triaged accurately by the per-task reviews; nothing was under-reported. The branch matches the plan task-for-task with no scope creep.

### Assessment

**Ready to merge?** Yes.

**Reasoning:** All 86 tests pass against a live DB + filesystem + FakeExecutor, lint/format are clean, and the implementation matches the plan exactly with correct ordering (validate+quota before any write), airtight ownership/hidden filtering, and clean Storage/Executor seams that Plans 6-8 can build on. The remaining items are downstream-contract notes (quota atomicity, executor-exception handling, `execute_run` state guard) that are correctly out of scope for the transport-agnostic core and belong to Plans 6-7; the `_reset_to_base` test guard is adequate. No critical or merge-blocking issues.</result>

### Strengths

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`service.py` line 60 — premature `finished_at` before executor call (stale timestamp on success)**

```python
run.finished_at = datetime.datetime.now(datetime.UTC)   # &lt;-- set here, BEFORE executor runs
try:
    result = await asyncio.to_thread(executor.execute, request)
except Exception as exc:
    run.status = RunStatus.FAILED
    run.error = f"executor error: {exc}"
    run.finished_at = datetime.datetime.now(datetime.UTC)   # overwritten correctly in except
    ...

run.finished_at = datetime.datetime.now(datetime.UTC)   # overwritten correctly in success path
```

On the success (and clean-failure) path the pre-try assignment is immediately overwritten, so it has no observable effect and the committed value is correct. However the pre-try assignment is dead code that could mislead a future reader into thinking `finished_at` marks when the job was *submitted* to the thread, not when it *finished*. It also means that if someone removes the post-try assignment while refactoring, the persisted timestamp will be wrong.

This matches the spec as written (the brief's code contains the same pattern), so this is not a deviation — but it is a latent defect worth cleaning up. Fix: remove the pre-try `run.finished_at` line (diff line 60); only the in-except and post-try assignments are needed.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

### Strengths

- **`try_allocate` atomicity is correct**: the guard `if count &gt; len(self._free): return None` at `pool.py:50` checks before any mutation. State is only modified after the guard passes, so a failed allocation provably leaves `_free` unchanged.
- **Zero-count edge case is handled without a special branch**: `sorted(self._free)[:0]` returns `[]`, and `difference_update([])` is a no-op — elegant and implicitly correct.
- **`release` correctly filters to pool-owned IDs** (`pool.py:58`): `if gpu_id in self._all` prevents accepting IDs that were never registered, closing the only realistic corruption vector.
- **`_free` as a `set` and `_all` as a `list`**: appropriate data structures — O(1) membership for `_free`, stable ordering preserved in `_all` for filter semantics in `release`.
- **Minimal, YAGNI-clean implementation**: no speculative thread-safety, no extra helpers, no dead code.
- **Tests are taken verbatim from the spec**, satisfying the brief exactly and ensuring no semantic drift.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

None.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`pool.py:36` — `__init__` has no docstring.**
`can_allocate`, `try_allocate`, `release`, and the class all have docstrings, but `__init__` does not. The global constraint requires Google-style docstrings on all public classes and functions. `__init__` with a non-trivial body (two assignments, both with semantic meaning) warrants at least a one-liner explaining the parameters. Fix:
```python
def __init__(self, gpu_ids: list[int]) -&gt; None:
    """Initialise the pool with the given GPU IDs, all marked free."""
    self._all = list(gpu_ids)
    self._free = set(gpu_ids)
```

**`pool.py:46` — `can_allocate(0)` returns `True` even though `available` may be 0.**
This is technically correct (0 GPUs are always allocatable), but it could surprise callers who use `can_allocate` as a pre-check before calling `try_allocate`. The current docstring says "Whether `count` GPUs are currently free", which holds for count=0. No fix strictly required, but a note in the docstring ("Always True for count=0") would eliminate potential confusion.

---

### Strengths

- **Lock scope is correct**: `of=Run` ensures only `runs` rows are locked, not `tools` rows, which is the right behavior to avoid unnecessary contention on a mostly-static table.
- **Pool atomicity under skipped runs**: `pool.try_allocate` is only called; if it returns `None` the pool is not mutated and the loop continues — no partial allocation leaks.
- **`session.refresh(run)` after commit**: correctly re-synchronizes the ORM object with DB state (server-side defaults, timestamps) before returning.
- **Tests use real Postgres**: `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` and `ARRAY` column types are Postgres-specific; SQLite would silently mis-test both.
- **`pytestmark = pytest.mark.integration`**: integration tests are correctly marked so they can be gated in CI.
- **`_tool` uses keyword-only `gpu_count`**: `*` in the signature prevents positional misuse in test helpers.
- **No YAGNI**: no config knobs, no extra helpers, no over-engineering.

---

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`claim.py:46` — All candidate rows fetched into memory before iteration**

`rows = (await session.execute(stmt)).all()` materializes the entire locked result set into a Python list before the loop starts. This is fine for correctness, but it means every QUEUED row is locked for the duration of the transaction, even rows far down the list that will never be claimed. For a small scheduler this is unlikely to matter, but it directly impacts concurrency: a second scheduler instance trying to claim a different run that happens to be in this locked batch will be blocked until this transaction commits.

The spec doesn't prohibit this pattern, so it is not a spec violation, but the intent of `SKIP LOCKED` is to support concurrent claiming — materializing all rows defeats some of that benefit. Consider using `.scalars()` with server-side cursor / `yield_per` or streaming execution if concurrent scheduler instances are expected.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`claim.py:31` — Function signature line length**

`async def claim_runnable_run(session: AsyncSession, pool: GpuPool) -&gt; tuple[Run, list[int]] | None:` is 95 characters — within the 100-char limit, so not a violation. No action needed; noted for awareness.

**`test_claim.py:88` — `_tool` name collides if `gpu_count` varies within one test**

`name=f"t{gpu_count}"` means two calls with the same `gpu_count` would hit a unique-name constraint. This is fine for the current test suite (each test creates one tool), but would silently break if a future test needed two tools with identical GPU counts. A `uuid` suffix would be more robust. Minor ergonomic point only.

**`test_claim.py:80-85` — `_user` helper commits separately per test setup call**

Each helper (`_user`, `_tool`, `_queue`) issues its own `session.commit()`. This is correct and clear, but three separate commits per test adds latency. A single fixture that bulk-inserts all setup objects would be faster. This is purely cosmetic for a test suite this size.

### Strengths

- `sub_timeout = request.timeout + 60` elegantly ensures Python's watchdog always fires after autobio's own internal timeout, preventing hung processes while keeping the margin explicit and reasoned.
- Error capture falls back gracefully: `(proc.stderr or proc.stdout or "autobio run failed")[-_ERROR_TAIL:]` — both channels covered, bounded, and never empty.
- `_gpu_seconds` as a `@staticmethod` is correct — no instance state needed, and it's reused in both the `TimeoutExpired` branch and the normal path, eliminating duplication.
- The `shutil.move` loop is simple and correct for moving directory contents (not the directory itself) into `outputs_dir`, exactly matching what autobio's layout requires.
- The monkeypatch in `test_success_moves_outputs` reconstructs autobio's actual workspace layout (`workspace/outputs/raw/emb.npy`) and verifies the file lands at `request.outputs_dir/raw/emb.npy` — a meaningful end-to-end assertion, not just a success flag check.
- Wall time measured with `time.monotonic()` — immune to clock adjustments.

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`autobio_executor.py:85–88` — Silent success when `workspace/outputs/` does not exist**

```python
autobio_outputs = workspace / "outputs"
if autobio_outputs.is_dir():
    for item in autobio_outputs.iterdir():
        shutil.move(str(item), str(request.outputs_dir / item.name))
return ExecutionResult(succeeded=True, ...)
```

If autobio exits 0 but produces no `outputs/` directory (a misconfigured run, a tool that wrote nothing, or a future autobio version that changed its layout), the executor returns `succeeded=True` with an empty `outputs_dir`. The caller will have no signal that outputs are missing. The brief says "on success moves autobio's `outputs/` into `request.outputs_dir`" — implying outputs are expected. At minimum, log a warning; ideally, treat a missing `outputs/` dir after a zero exit as a suspicious condition (warn, or optionally fail). Fix: replace the bare `if` with a check that raises or returns a failed result when the dir is absent, or at least logs via `logging.warning`.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`autobio_executor.py:88` — `shutil.move` with `str()` conversions are unnecessary in Python 3.9+**

`shutil.move(str(item), str(request.outputs_dir / item.name))` — `shutil.move` has accepted `Path` objects since 3.9; the global constraint is Python ≥3.11. The `str()` wrapping is harmless but inconsistent with the style guide's "use `Path` objects throughout; only call `str()` at IO boundaries" preference. Fix: `shutil.move(item, request.outputs_dir / item.name)`.

**`tests/test_autobio_executor.py:142–143` — `_fake_run` helper signatures missing type hints**

```python
def _fake_run(cmd, **kwargs):
    return subprocess.CompletedProcess(cmd, returncode=1, stdout="", stderr="boom")
```

Both `_fake_run` closures lack type annotations. The style guide requires type hints on all function signatures. Fix: `def _fake_run(cmd: list[str], **kwargs: object) -&gt; subprocess.CompletedProcess[str]:`.

**`tests/test_autobio_executor.py` — no test for `TimeoutExpired` path**

The timeout handling is a distinct code path (`autobio_executor.py:68–75`) that is not covered by any unit test. The brief does not explicitly require a timeout test, but the code path is non-trivial (wall time still computed, `gpu_seconds` still set). A `monkeypatch` test raising `subprocess.TimeoutExpired` would close this gap.

The only issue worth fixing before shipping is the silent-success when `workspace/outputs/` is absent, which could mask misconfigured runs.</result>
