---

### Spec Compliance

- ✅ `config.py`: `gpu_count: int = 8` and `scheduler_poll_interval: float = 2.0` added after `storage_root`, exact position and defaults match brief.
- ✅ `Scheduler.__init__` signature: keyword-only params `sessionmaker`, `executor`, `storage`, `gpu_pool`, `poll_interval` — matches brief exactly.
- ✅ `run_once`: reaps first (`self._reap()`), then checks maintenance, then loops `claim_runnable_run` — order is correct.
- ✅ `_reap`: only releases GPUs for `task.done()` tasks and removes them from `_inflight`. Iterates over `list(self._inflight.items())` so dict mutation during iteration is safe.
- ✅ `_dispatch`: opens a fresh session per call via `self._sessionmaker()` as a context manager. Loads `Run` by PK, then calls `execute_run`. Each dispatch gets its own session — no shared session across concurrent tasks.
- ✅ `drain`: collects tasks, `asyncio.gather(*tasks, return_exceptions=True)`, then `_reap()`. Absorbs failures without re-raising.
- ✅ `run_forever`: infinite `while True: run_once + sleep`.
- ✅ `tests/scheduler/test_service.py`: both tests from brief present; ruff-mandated import reordering (`Run, RunStatus` not `RunStatus, Run`) and `.scalars().all()` line-wrap applied correctly.
- ✅ `pytestmark = pytest.mark.integration` set.
- ✅ All global constraints met: `from __future__ import annotations`, type hints on all signatures, Google docstrings on all public methods, absolute imports, line length within 100 chars.

---

### Strengths

- **Session isolation is correct**: `_dispatch` uses `async with self._sessionmaker() as session` — each concurrent task gets its own transaction. This is the right pattern for concurrent async SQLAlchemy work and prevents session-sharing bugs that would cause hard-to-diagnose failures under load.
- **Mutation-safe reap**: `list(self._inflight.items())` defensively copies the dict view before iterating and deleting — avoids `RuntimeError: dictionary changed size during iteration`.
- **`return_exceptions=True` in drain**: task failures do not prevent GPU release; `_reap` runs after gather regardless, so GPUs are always freed on drain even when tasks fail.
- **`run_once` session scope is correct**: the claim loop runs inside a single session (good for transactional claim semantics), while execution happens in separate per-dispatch sessions (good for concurrency). These are the right boundaries.
- **No GPU leak on failed dispatch**: if `execute_run` raises, the asyncio task transitions to done with an exception; `_reap` checks `task.done()` (which is True for cancelled/failed tasks, not just successful ones), so GPUs are released correctly regardless of outcome. This is the critical correctness property for a GPU scheduler.

---

### Issues

#### Critical (Must Fix)

None.

#### Important (Should Fix)

**`service.py:86-91` — silent no-op if run is not found in `_dispatch`**

```python
run = await session.get(Run, run_id)
if run is not None:
    await execute_run(session, run, self._executor, self._storage)
```

If `session.get` returns `None` (row deleted between claim and dispatch — shouldn't happen in normal operation, but can happen in tests or under unusual DB conditions), the run stays in `RUNNING` status forever (it was claimed by `claim_runnable_run` before `_dispatch` was called), and its GPUs are still released by `_reap` once the task finishes. The run becomes a zombie: `RUNNING` with no task. This won't cause a GPU leak, but it will cause a stuck run that can never be re-queued. A `logging.warning` or an explicit status reset to `FAILED` would be appropriate here.

**`service.py:79-84` — `_reap` does not log task exceptions**

`drain` uses `return_exceptions=True`, which is correct, but neither `drain` nor `_reap` logs or surfaces exceptions from failed tasks. If `execute_run` raises unexpectedly, the failure is silently swallowed. In production this would make debugging very difficult. At minimum, `_reap` should inspect `task.exception()` for done-but-not-cancelled tasks and log it.

#### Minor (Nice to Have)

**`service.py:108-113` — `drain` snapshot vs. new arrivals**

`drain` snapshots `self._inflight.values()` at call time. If `run_once` is called concurrently while `drain` is awaiting (unlikely in current usage, but possible with `run_forever`), tasks added after the snapshot are not awaited by the current `drain` call and will be reaped on the next `_reap` call. The brief's intent is graceful shutdown, and in the tests drain is always called after `run_once` completes, so this is not a practical issue — just worth noting if `drain` is ever exposed as a true shutdown hook in a concurrent context.

**`tests/scheduler/test_service.py:169` — `test_run_once_dispatches_up_to_capacity` relies on timing-sensitive ordering**

The test asserts `pool.available == 2` after `drain()`, which is correct. But the second `run_once()` call relies on `drain()` having already updated `_inflight` (via `_reap`) so that there are no stale inflight entries blocking the third claim. This works correctly because `drain` calls `_reap` as its last step. This is fine, just not immediately obvious to a reader — a brief comment explaining why `drain` reaps would help.

---

### Assessment

**Task quality:** Approved

**Reasoning:** The implementation is a verbatim, correctly-applied copy of the brief's reference design; all spec requirements are met, the async orchestration is correct (reap-before-claim order, fresh session per dispatch, `return_exceptions=True` in drain, GPU release on task failure), and global code-quality constraints are satisfied. The two flagged "Important" items (silent no-op on missing run, swallowed task exceptions) are defensive-programming gaps rather than correctness bugs in the happy path, and neither causes a GPU leak.</result>

<result>Confirmed. `try_allocate` mutates the pool at line 31, and if `session.commit()` at line 37 (or `session.refresh` at line 38) raises, the allocated GPU IDs are never returned to the pool. This is a genuine GPU-leak window that requires no crash — just a commit failure (serialization error, connection blip, constraint violation). The `except Exception` boundary in `execute_run` protects the *execution*, but the *claim* has no such protection.

Let me also verify the impact of the second issue I want to confirm as blocking-vs-nit: if `run_once` raises anywhere, `run_forever` has no try/except, so the whole scheduler daemon exits. Combined with the pool leak, this compounds. Let me now check: is there a rollback anywhere that would return GPUs? No — the pool is pure in-memory Python state, untouched by DB rollback.

Now I'm confident in my findings. Let me also verify the `iterdir()` during `shutil.move` mutation concern — iterating a directory while moving items out of it. `iterdir()` returns a generator; moving items out of the directory being iterated can cause undefined iteration behavior on some platforms. Let me note that as a non-blocking robustness nit (materializing the list first is safer).

I have completed my analysis. Here is the review.

---

**Verdict:** Ship with nits

The branch is well-structured and the core spec claims hold up under tracing: the claim is atomically ordered under `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED (of=Run)`, `execute_run` is genuinely exception-safe at the execution boundary, GPU release is correctly keyed off dispatch-task completion (independent of run outcome), maintenance mode reaps but never claims, and crash recovery runs before the loop with no live dispatch to race. There is one real GPU-accounting gap in the claim path plus a couple of resilience nits. None are severe enough to block on their own, but the first is worth fixing before this owns real GPUs.

### Blocking (must fix before merge)

None strictly blocking. The item below is a real defect I'd strongly prefer fixed pre-merge; calling it high-priority non-blocking since the single-process, low-poll-rate deployment makes the trigger rare.

### Non-blocking (should fix)

1. **CONFIRMED — `scheduler/claim.py:31-38` — GPU leak if the claim commit fails.** `pool.try_allocate(gpu_count)` (line 31) mutates the in-memory pool *before* `await session.commit()` (line 37). If the commit or the subsequent `session.refresh(run)` (line 38) raises — serialization failure, connection blip, statement timeout, any `SQLAlchemyError` — the GPUs are already removed from `_free` but are never returned, and the run stays QUEUED. No crash is required; a single failed commit permanently shrinks the pool for the process lifetime. The `except Exception` boundary in `execute_run` protects execution but nothing protects the claim.
   Failure scenario: two overlapping DB operations cause a serialization error on `commit()` → `claim_runnable_run` raises → GPUs [0] gone from pool forever, run still QUEUED (correct in DB), pool now permanently at 7. Repeat and the node starves.
   Fix: wrap the mutate→commit in try/except and release on failure, e.g.

   ```python
   gpu_ids = pool.try_allocate(gpu_count)
   if gpu_ids is None:
       continue
   try:
       run.status = RunStatus.RUNNING
       run.assigned_gpu_ids = gpu_ids
       run.started_at = datetime.datetime.now(datetime.UTC)
       await session.commit()
       await session.refresh(run)
   except Exception:
       pool.release(gpu_ids)
       await session.rollback()
       raise
   return run, gpu_ids
   ```

2. **CONFIRMED — `scheduler/service.py:81-85` — `run_forever` has no error guard.** Any exception from `run_once` (e.g. a transient `get_system_settings`/DB error, or the claim exception above) propagates out of `run_forever` and kills the daemon. The recovery-on-restart path exists, but a bare transient blip shouldn't take the whole scheduler down. Consider a try/except around `await self.run_once()` that logs and continues after the poll sleep. This also bounds the blast radius of finding #1 (a leaked GPU) to "reduced capacity" rather than "dead scheduler."

3. **CONFIRMED — `autobio_executor.py:70-71` — mutating a directory while iterating it.** `for item in autobio_outputs.iterdir(): shutil.move(item, ...)` removes entries from `autobio_outputs` while its `iterdir()` generator is live. This is unspecified behavior for `os.scandir`-backed iteration and can skip files on some filesystems. Materialize first: `for item in list(autobio_outputs.iterdir()):`.

4. **PLAUSIBLE — `autobio_executor.py:71` — `shutil.move` clobber on name collision.** If `request.outputs_dir / item.name` already exists (retry of a run into a non-empty outputs dir, or a name that collides with an existing subdir), `shutil.move` nests a directory inside the existing one or overwrites a file. Fresh runs have an empty `outputs_dir` so the normal path is safe; only worth a guard if reruns into a populated dir are ever possible. No traversal risk — names come from autobio's own `outputs/` children, joined via `/ item.name` (single path component).

5. **CONFIRMED (documented assumption, not a code bug) — cross-process GPU coordination.** The spec's "atomic … across concurrent schedulers" is satisfied only for *run* claiming (SKIP LOCKED prevents double-claim). *GPU assignment* lives entirely in the per-process in-memory `GpuPool`; two scheduler processes would each think all 8 GPUs are free and could co-assign GPU 0. This is fine under the stated single-process invariant, but nothing in the code *enforces* single-process (no advisory lock / leader election). Worth a one-line comment or a `pg_advisory_lock` guard in `main.py` so a second accidental `fold-scheduler` can't silently double-book GPUs.

### Verified strengths

- **Atomic claim, no double-claim:** `select(...).with_for_update(skip_locked=True, of=Run)` scoped to `Run` (not `Tool`), filtered to `QUEUED`, ordered by `created_at`. After each claim commits, the row is RUNNING so the next fresh `SELECT` in the `while` loop cannot re-select it — no double-claim within a cycle, and SKIP LOCKED prevents a sibling worker grabbing the same row. Lock is correctly on `Run` only, so the shared `Tool` row isn't locked (avoids serializing all runs of one tool). Confirmed correct.
- **GPU release exactly once per terminal outcome:** release is keyed on dispatch-*task* completion in `_reap` (line 43-48), which fires for success, failure, executor exception, timeout, and even the `run is None` skip path — every path drives the task to `done()` exactly once, then `del self._inflight[run_id]` prevents a second release. `_reap` runs both in `run_once` and `drain`. No double-free, no per-branch leak. Confirmed correct.
- **Never stuck RUNNING:** `execute_run` requires RUNNING (guards other states with `InvalidRunState`), and the single documented `except Exception` at the `asyncio.to_thread` boundary marks FAILED + `finished_at` + commits. `_dispatch` uses its own session and `session.get` sees the committed RUNNING row (`expire_on_commit=False` across sessions). Confirmed correct.
- **Maintenance mode:** read from DB each `run_once` via `get_system_settings`; `_reap()` runs *before* the maintenance check so in-flight dispatches still free GPUs, and the early `return` claims/dispatches nothing. Confirmed correct.
- **Crash recovery:** `fail_orphaned_runs` runs before `run_forever` when no dispatch is in flight (fresh process, freshly-constructed all-free pool), touches only `status == RUNNING`, leaves QUEUED/SUCCEEDED untouched. No race with live dispatch. Confirmed correct.
- **Executor robustness:** no `shell=True`, list-arg `subprocess.run` with explicit `timeout` (tool timeout + 60s grace), `TimeoutExpired` → FAILED, stderr (fallback stdout) surfaced and tail-bounded to 4000 chars, missing `outputs/` handled via `is_dir()` guard. `gpu_seconds` correctly `None` when no GPUs. Confirmed correct.</result>

### Issues (Critical / Important / Minor)
**Minor** — `src/fold_at_scripps/storage.py:93`: `write_input` returns `f"inputs/{path.name}"` using `path.name` rather than the original `filename` argument. If `filename` ever contains subdirectory separators (e.g. `"sub/dir.txt"`), `path.name` would silently collapse the returned relative path to just the basename (`"inputs/dir.txt"`), while the file is actually written at `inputs/sub/dir.txt`, causing the returned path to not resolve to the written file. Not exercised by any test and not forbidden by `input_path`'s traversal guard (which only blocks escaping the base dir, not subdirectories within it). Low real-world risk since callers are expected to pass plain filenames, but it's a latent mismatch between the returned path and the actual write location. Fix: return `f"inputs/{filename}"` or compute relative path via `path.relative_to(self.run_root(run_id))`.

**Reasoning:** Implementation matches the brief exactly (interfaces, guard reuse, idempotency, tests), lint/format are clean, and the one identified issue is a low-probability edge case with no test coverage requirement in the brief — not a blocker.</result>

<result>No lines over 100 chars. All constraints satisfied. I have completed my analysis.

### Spec Compliance — ✅

Every spec item is met and traced to the diff:
- ✅ `InputFile` frozen dataclass, `filename: str`/`content: bytes` — service.py:41-46 (diff).
- ✅ `submit_run(session, *, user, tool, params, storage, inputs=None) -&gt; Run`; `inputs: Sequence[InputFile] | None = None` (no mutable default) — service.py:48-56.
- ✅ Order: `validate_params` → `FOR UPDATE` on user row → `check_quota` → insert. Lock precedes quota check — service.py:69, 76-78.
- ✅ Stages each input via `storage.write_input`, records absolute path via `storage.input_path` — service.py:88-90.
- ✅ Config written with `_resolve_input_paths`; `Run.params` gets raw `params` (filenames); `output_dir` set — service.py:80, 91-92.
- ✅ Post-creation failure → `session.rollback()` + `storage.remove_run_dir(run_id)` + re-raise — service.py:94-98.
- ✅ `_resolve_input_paths` rewrites only top-level `format:"path"` fields whose value names an uploaded file (`isinstance(spec, dict)`, `format=="path"`, `key in resolved`, `value in staged`) — service.py:37-44.
- ✅ Tests match the brief: staging/resolution assertions (filename kept in `run.params`, absolute path in config.json) and the concurrency test asserting `["ok","quota"]` + count==1 with a second engine. Existing no-input tests preserved.

### Strengths
- The root-cause discovery is genuine and correctly diagnosed. The pre-savepoint `get_system_settings` did `commit()` on first access; SQLAlchemy's async commit ends the transaction and releases the `FOR UPDATE` lock — a real, silent defeat of the TOCTOU fix on any cold database. The report's bisection (raw-SQL lock works; full `submit_run` doesn't; pre-seeded settings fixes it) is sound methodology.
- The SAVEPOINT fix is the correct tool. I confirmed the two load-bearing PostgreSQL semantics: (a) releasing/rolling-back a savepoint does **not** release row locks acquired by the *outer* transaction, so the `FOR UPDATE` survives; (b) `async with session.begin_nested()` rolls back only the nested insert on `IntegrityError`, leaving the outer transaction alive and the caller's already-loaded `user`/`tool` objects un-expired (unlike a full `session.rollback()`, which was the earlier broken attempt described in the report). The `IntegrityError` re-fetch path is correct and the `if settings is None` guard is appropriately defensive.
- The cleanup boundary (`except Exception: rollback + remove_run_dir; raise`) re-raises rather than swallowing — a legitimate cleanup-and-propagate boundary, not a silenced exception.
- Line length, no mutable defaults, absolute imports, Google-style docstrings, `from __future__ import annotations` all satisfied (verified no line &gt;100 in all three files).

### Issues

**Confirmed — CONCURRENCY (verdict: no remaining hole).** I traced both interleavings under READ COMMITTED with a fresh DB:
- Steady state (settings exist): T2's `FOR UPDATE` on the user row blocks until T1 commits its QUEUED run; T2 then counts 1 ≥ 1 → `QuotaExceeded`. Symmetric for the reverse order. The count is *always* taken while holding the exclusive user-row lock, and the competing insert is committed before that lock releases. No window where both pass.
- Cold path: both `get_system_settings` calls may race on the PK insert; the loser blocks on the uncommitted PK, then gets `IntegrityError` and re-fetches. This happens *before* the `FOR UPDATE`, so it does not corrupt the quota gate. No remaining quota-exceed window; no lock released early.

**Minor — service.py:71-74 (pre-lock `get_system_settings` call is now redundant, and its comment is stale). CONFIRMED.**
- What's wrong: The comment says `get_system_settings()` "would otherwise commit to persist its defaults, which would release the row lock below." After Fix B, `get_system_settings` **no longer commits** — it uses a SAVEPOINT with no commit. So the stated justification for calling it before the lock no longer holds. Were this call deleted, the first-ever `get_system_settings` would run inside `check_quota` *after* the lock, and releasing its savepoint would NOT release the outer `FOR UPDATE` — correctness would be preserved either way.
- Failure scenario: none functional. This is purely a maintenance hazard — a future reader trusts a comment that describes behavior the code no longer has, and may "simplify" incorrectly or misunderstand the invariant.
- Residual (non-correctness) value worth noting: keeping the call pre-lock moves the cold-path SAVEPOINT insert — which can block on the PK conflict when two callers race — *outside* the `FOR UPDATE` critical section, marginally shortening how long the user-row lock is held on a cold DB. That is an optimization, not a requirement.
- Fix (optional): either (a) delete the pre-lock call and let `check_quota`'s `get_system_settings` handle first-access (simpler; relies solely on the savepoint invariant), or (b) keep it but rewrite the comment to state the real reason — "resolve/create the singleton before locking so the (potentially blocking) cold-path insert does not extend the user-row lock hold time" — and drop the stale "would otherwise commit / release the row lock" claim.

No Critical or Important issues found.

### Assessment
**Task quality:** Approved
**Reasoning:** All spec items are met and verified against the diff. The out-of-scope `system_settings.py` change is legitimate, correctly diagnosed, and correctly implemented — I independently confirmed the two PostgreSQL semantics it relies on (savepoint release does not drop outer-transaction row locks; `begin_nested` rollback leaves the outer transaction and loaded objects intact). I traced both concurrency interleavings on a cold and warm database and found no remaining quota-exceed window and no early lock release. The only finding is Minor: the pre-lock `get_system_settings` call is now redundant for correctness and its comment is stale (describes pre-savepoint commit behavior). That is a maintenance nit, not a trust issue, and does not block approval. Recommend the implementer address the stale comment (option b) or remove the redundant call (option a).</result>

### Strengths

- Exception mapping is clean: both `InvalidParams` and `QuotaExceeded` handlers use `raise ... from exc`, preserving the exception chain — no swallowed tracebacks, no bare/broad `except`.
- Returning `get_run(session, user, run.id)` instead of the bare `submit_run` result correctly avoids a `MissingGreenlet` risk on `RunRead` serialization, since `submit_run`'s returned `Run` (post `session.refresh`) would have lazy `tool`/`artifacts` relationships, while `get_run` eager-loads both via `selectinload` (`runs/service.py:126-131`).
- `f.filename` is correctly treated as `str | None` — the `if f.filename` guard in the list comprehension (`runs.py:103`) prevents constructing an `InputFile` with a `None` filename, which would violate `InputFile.filename: str` (`runs/service.py:24-29`).
- `files: list[UploadFile] = File(default=[])` is correct FastAPI idiom (per review instructions, not a mutable-default defect).
- Correctly relies on `get_enabled_tool` returning `None` uniformly for both missing and disabled tools, collapsing what could've been two branches into one 404 check.
- Report is honest and calibrated: explicitly notes the pre-existing `HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY` deprecation warning is a Starlette naming issue unrelated to behavior, and declines to "fix" it outside brief scope — correct judgment call.

### Issues

**Critical:** none.

**Important:** none. The one theoretical risk flagged in the review prompt — `get_run` returning `None` into a `response_model=RunRead` route — is not reachable on this endpoint's happy path: `run.id` at `runs.py:114` is the id of a `Run` just created and committed for this exact `user` within the same request (`submit_run` sets `user_id=user.id` at `runs/service.py:81`), so `get_run`'s `WHERE user_id == user.id AND hidden_at IS NULL` (`runs/service.py:128`) is guaranteed to match. No guard is needed here; this is correctly unguarded rather than defectively unguarded.

**Minor:**
- `runs.py:103` — `inputs = [InputFile(filename=f.filename, content=await f.read()) for f in files if f.filename]` reads every uploaded file fully into memory before staging. Fine for the current use case (small structure files) and not a regression from the brief (which specifies this exact pattern) — flagging only as a latent scalability note for large files, not a defect in this task.
- `models/artifact.py:29` declares `size_bytes: Mapped[int | None]` (nullable at the DB/ORM level), while `schemas/runs.py` (per brief) declares `ArtifactRead.size_bytes: int` (non-nullable). In practice `Artifact` rows are only ever created via `runs/service.py:210-219` using `StoredFile.size_bytes: int` (non-optional, from `path.stat().st_size`), so this can't currently produce a `None`→validation-error mismatch. This is a pre-existing model/schema nullability mismatch outside this task's diff (model and brief both predate this task), not something the implementer introduced or should have fixed here.
- Pre-existing Starlette `StarletteDeprecationWarning` on `HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY` (used per brief spec) — correctly left alone per report's reasoning; noted only for completeness, not actionable within this task.

So the constant likely emits a DeprecationWarning but is still functional (Minor #4 confirmed as a real-but-non-blocking warning). The suite is green, so it's not raising an error.

I have traced all four focus areas. Let me compile the review. Let me do one final verification on a potential emergent concern I noticed: the `submit` endpoint reads all files into memory and only filters `if f.filename`. If two uploaded files share the same `filename`, `write_input` overwrites the first with the second, and `staged[filename]` points to the last write — silent data loss but not a crash. Non-blocking edge case. Also, `f.filename` empty-string files are skipped (good, avoids the `File(default=[])` sentinel producing a phantom empty upload).

I now have a complete picture.

**Verdict:** Ship it

The branch is a clean, correct HTTP adapter over the existing run services. I traced every focus area end-to-end; the two carried-in correctness fixes (atomic quota, cancel 404/409) are genuinely sound, and no path releases the submit lock early. Nothing blocks merge.

### Blocking (must fix before merge)
None. I looked specifically for a lock-release window, a claimable-run-without-inputs window, a cancel/claim race, a traversal or ownership hole, and a lazy-load/MissingGreenlet on any Run-serializing route, and confirmed each is handled.

### Non-blocking (should / nice) — with triage of the 4 logged Minors

- **Minor 1 (`write_input` returns `inputs/{path.name}` vs `{filename}`)** — WON'T FIX (accept). CONFIRMED harmless: `submit_run` ignores the return value entirely (it builds `staged[...]` from `storage.input_path(...)`, not from this return), and `input_path`'s traversal guard already rejects separators before a subdir could form. Cosmetic inconsistency only.
- **Minor 2 (`ArtifactRead.size_bytes: int` vs `Artifact.size_bytes: int | None`)** — SHOULD FIX EVENTUALLY, non-blocking. CONFIRMED currently unreachable: the only Artifact creation site (`execute_run`, service.py:210-219) sources `size_bytes` from `StoredFile.size_bytes`, which is always `path.stat().st_size` (int). If any future path inserts a null size, Pydantic v2 will raise a `ValidationError` at serialization (500) on GET/detail. Prefer `size_bytes: int | None` on the schema (cheaper than a model NOT NULL + migration) to make the adapter robust to the model's declared nullability.
- **Minor 3 (`await f.read()` loads whole upload into memory)** — WON'T FIX now (correctly deferred to Plan 10). Acceptable for small structure files; the real mitigation is a request-body/upload size limit, which is out of this branch's scope.
- **Minor 4 (Starlette `HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY` deprecation)** — WON'T FIX now, non-blocking. CONFIRMED against the pinned Starlette 1.3.1: the constant is deprecated-but-functional (emits a DeprecationWarning; suite is green). Sweep it project-wide when you bump Starlette, not piecemeal here.

Additional non-blocking observations (emergent, not in the logged list):
- **`_resolve_input_paths` silent no-op on filename mismatch** (service.py:40-44) — PLAUSIBLE usability footgun, not a defect. A field is only rewritten when the param value string exactly equals an uploaded filename. If a user's `format:"path"` param names a file they didn't upload (or the upload's filename differs), the on-disk config keeps the literal relative string and autobio will fail to find it — but this fails gracefully (run → FAILED via `execute_run`), not silently or insecurely. Nothing validates that every required `format:"path"` param has a matching upload. Consider (future) validating this at submit time for a clearer 422 instead of a downstream FAILED run.
- **Duplicate upload filenames** (api/runs.py:125 → storage.write_input) — last-write-wins overwrite with no warning. Edge case; acceptable for now.
- **`submit` returns `get_run(...)` which is typed `Run | None`** (api/runs.py:136) — can't be None in practice (just committed, owned, non-hidden), but if it ever were, `response_model=RunRead` would serialize `null` at 201. Harmless; not worth guarding.

### Verified strengths (traced, not assumed)

- **Concurrency — submit (CONFIRMED).** `get_system_settings` is called before the `FOR UPDATE`, and its singleton creation is inside a `begin_nested()` SAVEPOINT with a flush (no commit) — so on a cold DB it cannot release the caller's locks. The `SELECT User.id … FOR UPDATE` (service.py:78) is held until `session.commit()` (service.py:94); `check_quota`'s second `get_system_settings` call hits the already-loaded row and commits nothing. Two concurrent same-user submits at the limit serialize on the user row, and the second's `count_in_flight_runs` sees the first's committed QUEUED run → exactly one passes. The `IntegrityError`-on-race fallback in `get_system_settings` is correct.
- **Concurrency — cancel (CONFIRMED).** Conditional `UPDATE … WHERE status=QUEUED` is atomic against the scheduler's `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` claim (claim.py:22-27): whichever commits the QUEUED→{CANCELED|RUNNING} transition first wins; `rowcount==0` → 409, correctly rolled back. `RunNotFound` (404) precedes the UPDATE and covers unknown/not-owned/hidden.
- **Staging seam (CONFIRMED).** Inputs are staged and config (with resolved absolute paths) is written *before* `session.commit()`, so a run only becomes claimable after its inputs exist on disk — no claimable-without-inputs window. The resolved config matches exactly what the frozen autobio executor consumes (`--config &lt;config_path&gt;`, autobio_executor.py:35-36). Failure path rolls back the transaction and best-effort removes the run dir. `Run.params` retains user filenames while config.json holds absolute paths — verified by `test_submit_stages_inputs_and_resolves_config_paths`.
- **Security / download (CONFIRMED).** Ownership-scoped via `get_run` (404, not 403 — verified by `test_download_requires_ownership`); restricted to indexed artifacts (`a.path == artifact_path`), so a traversal string matches no artifact and 404s before touching disk; plus defense-in-depth `outputs.resolve()` + `is_relative_to` + `is_file`. No endpoint leaks another user's data or server paths.
- **Eager-load discipline (CONFIRMED).** Every Run-serializing route (`submit`→`get_run`, `get_user_run`→`get_run`, `list_user_runs`→`list_runs`, `cancel_user_run`→`cancel_run`) uses `selectinload` for the relationships each schema touches (`RunSummary` needs `tool`; `RunRead` needs `tool`+`artifacts`). `cancel_run`'s post-UPDATE `session.refresh(run)` correctly reloads status and the already-loaded relationships under `expire_on_commit=False` — the green HTTP-level cancel test serializes `RunRead.artifacts` without MissingGreenlet. `soft_delete_run`'s return is discarded (204), so no serialization risk.</result>

### Spec Compliance — ✅

All interfaces match the brief exactly, confirmed by direct file reads (not just diff context):

- `admin/passwords.py:42-43` — `InvalidResetToken(Exception)`.
- `admin/passwords.py:46-48` — `_hash_token` = `hashlib.sha256(token.encode()).hexdigest()`.
- `admin/passwords.py:51-63` — `create_password_reset(session, *, actor, user_id, ttl=_DEFAULT_TTL) -&gt; tuple[str, PasswordResetToken]`. Token via `secrets.token_urlsafe(32)`; only `token_hash` stored (plaintext token never persisted, only returned); `expires_at = datetime.now(UTC) + ttl`; audits `user.password_reset_created`; raises `UserNotFound` via `get_user` (confirmed `src/fold_at_scripps/admin/users.py:28-33`).
- `admin/passwords.py:83-109` — `redeem_password_reset(session, *, token, new_password) -&gt; User`. Looks up by `_hash_token(token)`; rejects `row is None or row.used_at is not None or row.expires_at &lt;= now`; sets `hash_password(new_password)`; sets `used_at`; audits with `actor=None`; single-use enforced (second redeem hits `used_at is not None` → `InvalidResetToken`). Confirmed `record_audit`'s `actor` param is typed `User | None` (`audit.py:16`), so `actor=None` is a legitimate call, not a latent type violation.
- `ttl: datetime.timedelta = _DEFAULT_TTL` — module-level constant default, immutable type; no mutable-default-arg issue.
- `api/admin.py:159-174` — `POST /admin/users/{user_id}/password-reset` → 201 `PasswordResetResponse`; 404 on `UserNotFound`; `actor: User = Depends(require_admin)` declared, and the endpoint also inherits router-level `dependencies=[Depends(require_admin)]` (`api/admin.py:31`) — confirmed `require_admin` enforces `role is UserRole.ADMIN` else 403 (`auth/dependencies.py:33-39`).
- `api/auth.py:227-235` — `POST /auth/reset-password` → 204; 400 on `InvalidResetToken`. Confirmed the `/auth` router (`api/auth.py:25`) has **no** router-level auth dependency and the handler itself takes only `payload` and `session` — genuinely reachable unauthenticated, not accidentally admin-gated.
- Schemas match exactly: `PasswordResetResponse(token: str, expires_at: datetime.datetime)` (`schemas/admin.py:253-257`); `PasswordResetRedeem(token: str, new_password: str = Field(min_length=8))` (`schemas/auth.py:275-279`).
- Tests (`tests/api/test_admin_password_reset.py`) cover all four required scenarios with genuine assertions: admin-create→redeem→new-pw-login-200/old-pw-login-401; invalid token→400; unknown user→404; single-use (second redeem→400). Fixture `db_session` runs against a real async DB session with real password hashing and a real `/auth/login` round trip — not mocked.

### Strengths

- Minimal, faithful implementation with no scope creep beyond the brief.
- Timezone-aware handling is correct end-to-end: `datetime.now(datetime.UTC)` compared against `DateTime(timezone=True)` columns (confirmed `models/access.py:38-41`) — no naive/aware mismatch.
- `PasswordResetToken.token_hash` carries a DB-level `unique=True` constraint (`models/access.py:37`) — defense-in-depth beyond application logic.
- Import hygiene is correct: `api/admin.py:19` keeps the single existing `UserNotFound` import line (no duplicate); `api/auth.py` imports are cleanly extended as a parenthesized block.
- `hash_password` uses Argon2 via `pwdlib` (`PasswordHash.recommended()`) — a proper, salted, non-reversible KDF; the plaintext token itself is never stored anywhere, only handed back once in the response body as the spec requires.
- FK on `PasswordResetToken.user_id` has `ondelete="CASCADE"`, so the `user is None` `# pragma: no cover` branch in `redeem_password_reset` is currently unreachable by design, not an unguarded assumption.
- Report is honest and well-calibrated (flags the ruff-format cleanup, notes no background cleanup job as an accepted scope decision, notes an unrelated stale report file it overwrote).

**Verdict: Ship with nits**

The branch is coherent, well-tested, and the security-critical surfaces (admin gate, audit atomicity, password-reset, eager-loading, cancel race-safety) are correctly implemented. One real defect can 500 a mutating admin action, but it requires a &gt;64-char email and the failure is a clean rollback (no data corruption, no security hole). I'd fix it before merge but it does not block the architecture.

### Blocking (must fix before merge)

None that are architecturally blocking. The highest-severity issue (below, Minor 2) is a correctness bug worth fixing in this PR but degrades gracefully (500 + full rollback, no partial write, no audit gap), so I list it as the top non-blocking item rather than manufacture a blocker.

### Non-blocking (should / nice) — with triage of the 4 logged Minors

**Minor 2 — CONFIRMED, most severe. Should fix in this PR.**
`src/fold_at_scripps/models/audit.py:26` — `target_id` is `String(64)`; `src/fold_at_scripps/admin/access.py:97,122` pass `email` (a `String(320)` column, RFC max 254) as `target_id`. A registered/allowlisted email longer than 64 chars makes the audit-row flush raise `DataError` on Postgres, which rolls back the whole `add`/`remove` transaction → 500, and the allowlist mutation is lost. `add_allowed_email` accepts `EmailStr` with no length cap, so this is reachable by a valid input, not just abuse. SQLite (the test DB) does not enforce `String(64)`, which is exactly why the green suite can't see it — a genuine structural gap. Fix: store `str(entry.id)` as `target_id` and put the email in `details={"email": email}` (consistent with how `settings.update`/`user.update` already use `details`). Every other `target_id` in the branch is a UUID/`"1"`, so access.py is the lone offender.

**Minor 1 — CONFIRMED, acceptable to defer.** Allowlist `add` TOCTOU between the `select` existence check (access.py:87) and `commit`: two concurrent identical adds → one 500 (`IntegrityError`) instead of 409. Backed by the DB unique constraint (`models/access.py:19`), so no dup row is ever created; only the status code degrades under a rare concurrent-admin race. Note: the fix for Minor 2 (moving off email as target_id) does not fix this. Fine to leave; if touched, catch `IntegrityError` → 409.

**Minor 3 — cosmetic, defer.** 100-char line in `api/auth.py` and a pragma comment; ruff is clean at limit 100, so no action needed.

**Minor 4 — CONFIRMED cosmetic, optional.** `admin_cancel_run` (runs.py:334-353) does `session.get` for the None-check, then a conditional `UPDATE`, then `admin_get_run` reloads — up to 3 round-trips. The `get`-then-`UPDATE` split is actually load-bearing: it's what distinguishes 404 (no row) from 409 (row exists, not QUEUED), mirroring `runs/service.py::cancel_run`. The reload is needed because the bulk `UPDATE` doesn't refresh the ORM object and the response needs eager-loaded tool/user/artifacts. So the "2 queries for a None-check" framing understates why each query exists; it's fine as is. Two single-lined handler signatures vs the file's multi-line style is pure style.

Additional observations (all non-blocking, none new defects):
- `admin/runs.py:354` uses a bare `assert reloaded is not None`. Asserts can be stripped under `python -O`; here it only guards an invariant established one transaction earlier, so acceptable, but a defensive `raise RunNotFound` would be more robust than an assert on a request path.
- `create_password_reset` does not invalidate prior outstanding tokens for the same user — multiple valid reset tokens can coexist. Not a spec violation (each is single-use + expiring), but worth a product note.

### Verified strengths (traced)

- **Authorization is airtight (CONFIRMED).** The router is declared `APIRouter(prefix="/admin", …, dependencies=[Depends(require_admin)])` (`api/admin.py:522`), so every one of the 15 `/admin` routes inherits the gate regardless of whether the handler also injects `actor`. `require_admin` layers on `get_current_user` (`auth/dependencies.py:839-845`): 401 for anon/inactive, 403 for authenticated non-admin — covered by `test_list_users_requires_admin` (both 401 and 403) and the unit tests in `test_dependencies.py`. The one public exception, `POST /auth/reset-password`, is on the `auth` router with no admin dep — correct and intended.
- **Audit atomicity (CONFIRMED).** `record_audit` flushes but never commits (`audit.py:793`); each service adds its domain change + audit row then commits once (users/access/settings/catalog-toggle/passwords/runs). `trigger_sync` is the documented exception — `sync_catalog` commits (`catalog/service.py:55`), then the audit row is added and committed separately (`admin/catalog.py:177-184`) — matching the spec's stated carve-out. No mutation commits without an audit, and no audit commits without its mutation (they share the transaction), except that documented sync case.
- **Password-reset security (CONFIRMED).** Only the SHA-256 hash is persisted (`passwords.py:237`, `token_hash String(128)`); plaintext is returned once and never stored. Redemption checks `used_at is not None or expires_at &lt;= now` with tz-aware `datetime.now(datetime.UTC)` vs a `DateTime(timezone=True)` column (`passwords.py:262-263`) — no naive/aware mismatch. Single-use and expiry are covered by `test_reset_token_single_use` and the 400 path. Create is admin-gated; redeem returns a generic `400 "Invalid or expired reset token"` for unknown/expired/used alike, and the lookup is keyed by token hash (not email), so redemption leaks no information about which emails or tokens exist. No user enumeration.
- **Eager-load discipline (CONFIRMED).** Every Run-serializing route eager-loads what its response schema touches: `admin_list_runs` loads `tool`+`user` for `AdminRunSummary` (`runs.py:308`); `admin_get_run` loads `tool`+`user`+`artifacts` for `AdminRunRead` (`runs.py:322`); `admin_cancel_run` returns via `admin_get_run`, so the post-cancel response is fully loaded. `AdminUserRead`/`ToolAdminRead`/`SystemSettingsRead`/`AllowedEmailRead`/`AuditLogRead` are all scalar-only (no relationship traversal), so no lazy-load risk. No MissingGreenlet path.
- **Cancel race-safety (CONFIRMED).** `admin_cancel_run` uses conditional `UPDATE … WHERE id=? AND status=QUEUED` (`runs.py:337-341`), identical to the user-facing `cancel_run` and race-safe against the scheduler's claim; `rowcount==0` → rollback → 409, missing row → 404. 404/409 are distinct and tested.
- **Partial-update / mass-assignment safety (CONFIRMED).** Both `update_user` and `update_settings` iterate a private `_UPDATABLE` allow-list and apply only keys present in the `model_dump(exclude_unset=True)` payload (`users.py:454-457`, `settings.py:388-391`), so omitted fields are untouched and unknown keys cannot be injected. `AdminUserUpdate` allows explicit `max_concurrent_runs_override: null` to clear the override (nullable column), while omission leaves it — the intended distinction. Schema field/types match the models (checked `AdminUserRead`, `ToolAdminRead`, `SystemSettingsRead`, `AdminRunRead` against `user.py`/`tool.py`/`system.py`/`run.py`); all response schemas set `from_attributes=True`.
- Global constraints hold: `from __future__ import annotations` in every new module; absolute imports; no mutable default args; `except Exception` appears only at the documented executor boundary (unchanged code), not in this branch's admin services.

Files central to the review: `src/fold_at_scripps/api/admin.py`, `src/fold_at_scripps/auth/dependencies.py`, `src/fold_at_scripps/audit.py`, `src/fold_at_scripps/admin/{access,passwords,runs,settings,users,catalog}.py`, `src/fold_at_scripps/models/audit.py` (the `String(64)` seam), `src/fold_at_scripps/api/auth.py` (public redeem).</result>

<result>The commit exists already. Everything checks out against what I need. Now let me assess the tsconfig `paths` without `baseUrl` concern (TS behavior), which is a legitimate technical question worth confirming.

In TypeScript, `paths` mapping without `baseUrl` resolves relative to the config file itself (this became supported behavior once `baseUrl` was made optional — paths resolve relative to the `tsconfig.json` location). This is correct and intentional for modern TS. `tsconfig.app.json` sets `paths: {"@/*": ["./src/*"]}` and is located at `frontend/tsconfig.app.json`, so `./src/*` correctly resolves to `frontend/src/*`. This is consistent with Vite's `resolve.alias` mapping `@` → `path.resolve(__dirname, "./src")` in `vite.config.ts`. Both agree.

Now finalizing the review.

### Strengths

### Issues

**Important** — `frontend/vitest.environment.ts:29-39`. Restoring native `File`/`Blob`/`FormData`/`Request`/`Response`/`Headers` on top of jsdom creates a real class-identity split for *future* tests: anything constructed via `new File(...)`/`new Blob(...)`/`new FormData(...)` in test code is now Node-native, while anything jsdom generates internally (e.g., via `URL.createObjectURL`, native `&lt;input&gt;` file-change events assembled by hand with `document.createElement`, `DataTransfer`) remains jsdom-native. I verified `@testing-library/user-event`'s `upload()` helper (`utils/dataTransfer/FileList.js`, `utils/edit/setFiles.js`) works structurally with no `instanceof` brand checks, so RTL's own `userEvent.upload()` path is safe. But any later component/application code that does `x instanceof File` or `x instanceof Blob` for type-narrowing (a common React pattern for drag-and-drop upload widgets) will get inconsistent results in tests vs. real browsers. The report already flags this exact risk in its "Concerns" section — this is a known, disclosed trade-off, not an oversight, but it should be treated as a hard requirement for whoever writes the run-submission upload UI in a later task: don't use `instanceof File`/`Blob` for narrowing: use structural checks (`typeof x === "object" &amp;&amp; "name" in x`) or rely on the `File[]` type from the `&lt;input&gt;` element instead.

**Minor** — `frontend/vitest.environment.ts` has no unit test of its own (understandable — it's test infrastructure, and it's exercised indirectly by `api.test.ts`'s green multipart test), but there's no regression guard if a future vitest/jsdom upgrade changes `builtinEnvironments.jsdom`'s shape. Not blocking; just note for future maintainers.

**Minor** — `frontend/src/lib/api.ts:141`, `artifactUrl` doesn't URL-encode the `runId` segment (only the artifact `path` segments are encoded). Since `runId` is always a UUID string in practice (never user-controlled free text), this isn't currently exploitable, but it's a slight inconsistency with the "encode every path segment" principle applied to the rest of the URL.

### Assessment
**Task quality: Approved**

**Reasoning:** The type and client contract is verified correct not just against the brief but against the actual backend implementation (enums, Pydantic schemas, FastAPI routes, and the multipart `Form`/`File` signature) — zero drift found anywhere. The custom vitest environment is a well-scoped, well-investigated fix for a real (and reproducible, per the report's isolated repro) ecosystem gap; it correctly layers on top of jsdom rather than replacing it, is wired correctly, and is clean under the "no any" / ESLint constraints. The one Important-tier issue (native vs. jsdom `File`/`Blob` identity split for `instanceof` checks in later component tests) is real but already self-disclosed by the implementer with an accurate mitigation note, and doesn't affect this task's own contract since `submitRun` uses `File` only structurally. No fixes are required before merging; the disclosed risk should simply be carried forward as a constraint for the run-submission UI task.</result>

### Spec Compliance — ✅

- required → non-optional, else `.optional()` — ✅ (`build-zod.ts:55`)

**The array deviation — sound.** The brief's literal code (`else if (type==="array" &amp;&amp; items &amp;&amp; isScalar(items)) → z.array(item)`, else falls to blanket `z.unknown()`) would map ablang2's `sequences` (`type:"array"`, `items:{$ref:...}`, no `type` on items) to `z.unknown()`. Empirically verified in this review: required `z.unknown()` accepts `"notarray"` (`safeParse("notarray").success === true`), which would make the brief's own test (`sequences:"notarray"` → expect `false`) fail against the *real* fixture — the brief's prose describing ablang2 `sequences` as "a scalar array" was simply wrong; the real captured schema is array-of-$ref-objects. The implemented fix — route **any** `type:"array"` to `z.array(item)`, using the concrete scalar mapping when items are scalar and `z.array(z.unknown())` otherwise — was verified here to reject non-array values (`undefined`→false, `"notarray"`→false) while accepting valid arrays (`["EVQ"]`→true), and preserves the brief's scalar-item behavior for `chains_to_design`/`templates`. Correct, minimal, and consistent with the "server-authoritative" philosophy (element structure inside the array is left to `.unknown()`, but the outer array-ness is still enforced client-side).

### Strengths
- Fixtures cross-checked field-by-field against report claims; all real, all present in diff with correct required/anyOf/default shapes.
- `unwrapNullable` correctly requires exactly one non-null branch (`nonNull.length === 1`) before unwrapping — avoids misinterpreting arbitrary multi-type unions as simple nullable scalars.
- Multi-type `anyOf` (e.g. 3+ branches, or 2 non-null branches) degrades to `z.unknown()` rather than crashing or silently picking a wrong branch — verified by tracing `unwrapNullable` → falls through to `{inner: schema, nullable: false}` → `inner.type` undefined → final `else` in `fieldZod`. Sane, permissive fallback.
- `.nullable().optional()` composition verified empirically in this review: accepts `undefined`, accepts `null`, accepts valid value, rejects wrong type — exactly the required behavior for an optional-nullable field (ablang2 `layer`).
- No `any` anywhere; `JsonSchema` (Task 2, fully typed) used throughout; strict-mode-clean signature (`z.ZodTypeAny` / `z.ZodType` return types).
- Test suite genuinely exercises the required assertions: valid antifold payload, missing-required rejection, ablang2 null/omitted `layer`, ablang2 array-required + non-array rejection, inline enum restriction, boolean/integer-min mapping — all present and matching the brief.
- `.passthrough()` correctly leaves unknown keys (e.g. server-added fields) unrejected — intended, per brief.

### Issues
None rising to Critical or Important. Two Minor/cosmetic observations:

- **Minor** — `build-zod.ts:41`: for arrays-of-objects (e.g. ablang2 `sequences`), element-level required-ness (`AntibodySequence.required: ["id"]`) is entirely unvalidated client-side (`z.unknown()` per element). This is explicitly the intended, documented tradeoff (server-authoritative), not a bug — flagged only for completeness since it's a real gap in client-side UX (a malformed sequence object like `{}` inside the array would pass client validation and fail server-side instead). No fix needed per brief's own design.
- **Minor** — `build-zod.ts:25`: `Array.isArray(inner.enum) &amp;&amp; inner.enum.length &gt; 0` is checked before the `anyOf`-derived `inner` is checked for `type`. If a schema had both `enum` and a conflicting `type` (not present in any fixture here), enum wins silently. Matches brief intent (enum implies restricted string set) and no fixture exercises a conflict, so not a real defect — noted only as a latent ambiguity.

### Strengths

- Clean separation of concerns: `describe.ts` (pure classification logic) vs `SchemaForm.tsx` (rendering/state) vs `FileField`/`JsonField` (presentational). Matches the codebase's "factor heavy logic into named helpers" convention and keeps every function well under 50 lines.
- The intermediate-RED story in the report (native `&lt;details&gt;` keeps children mounted; `&lt;summary&gt;` doesn't map to role `button`) shows real TDD, not retrofitted tests — verified by reading the actual disclosure implementation, which is a plain controlled `&lt;button&gt;`, not a shadcn Collapsible/`&lt;details&gt;` wrapper.
- `filesRef` (uncommitted ref) + `fileNames`/`jsonText` (state for re-render) is a sensible split — avoids re-rendering on every keystroke of unrelated fields while still updating visible filename/JSON text.
- The `handleFileChange`'s redundant `form.setValue(name, file.name, { shouldValidate: true })` is a deliberate double-write (also validated at `handleFormSubmit:172-174`) that lets RHF/Zod validate the filename string itself (e.g. required-file-missing errors surface through RHF's own error state) — good defense in depth, not just dead code.
- `parseJsonFields` clears/sets errors per-field independently and `handleJsonChange` proactively `clearErrors` on edit, so a fixed-then-resubmitted JSON field doesn't leave a stale error message.

### Issues

**Important:** None found. No `instanceof File/Blob`, no `any`, correct widget selection across all three fixtures (including the array-of-`$ref`-objects case in `ablang2.json`, which isn't in the brief's mandatory 3 tests but is handled correctly by the fallback logic), files/JSON submit-blocking contract verified by tracing the code paths.

**Minor:**
1. `frontend/src/lib/schema-form/fields/describe.ts:9` (`FieldDescriptor.schema`) — the unwrapped inner schema is computed and stored on every descriptor but never consumed anywhere in `SchemaForm.tsx` or the field widgets. Dead data; harmless but should probably be dropped or actually used (e.g., for `min`/`max` on number inputs, which currently aren't surfaced from the schema at all even though `build-zod.ts` enforces them at validation time — a UX inconsistency: the Zod resolver will reject out-of-range numbers, but the `&lt;Input type="number"&gt;` has no `min`/`max` HTML attributes to hint the constraint).
2. `frontend/src/lib/schema-form/fields/FileField.tsx:68`, `JsonField.tsx:66`, `SchemaForm.tsx:263` — error `&lt;p&gt;` text is rendered but not referenced by `aria-describedby` (only the description paragraph is). Screen readers get `aria-invalid` but not the specific error text association. Concrete failure scenario: a screen-reader user tabs to an invalid field, hears only "invalid," not "Enter valid JSON."
3. `frontend/src/lib/schema-form/SchemaForm.tsx` — the Advanced panel uses a hardcoded `id="advanced-options-panel"` for `aria-controls` rather than a `useId()`-scoped id. Not a bug today (no page renders two `SchemaForm`s at once), but it's a latent duplicate-ID bug if a future page (e.g., a tool-comparison view) mounts the component twice.

### Issues

**Minor:**
- `frontend/src/pages/SubmitPage.tsx:177` — `mutationFn: ({ values, files }) =&gt; submitRun((tool as ToolRead).id, values, files)`. The `tool as ToolRead` cast is unnecessary: by the time `SchemaForm` (and thus a submit) can render, the component has already returned early on `isLoading`/`isError || !tool`, so `tool` is narrowed to `ToolRead` in that later code, but TypeScript can't see that narrowing carry into the `useMutation` call defined above the early return. This is a pre-existing narrowing limitation, not a bug — the cast is safe — but a cleaner alternative would be to move the mutation's `mutationFn` to close over `tool.id` freshly after the null-check, or memoize `tool.id` past the guard. Not worth blocking on; purely a style nit.
- `frontend/src/pages/SubmitPage.test.tsx:97-104` — the mocked `RunRead` response for `POST /runs` (and the `tool` object mock) is a plain object literal, not typed/asserted against `RunRead`/`ToolRead` (e.g. via `satisfies`), so a future field rename in `types/api.ts` wouldn't be caught by these tests at the type level. Cosmetic; consistent with how other test files in the suite appear to mock (per the brief's own suggested test code, which has the same characteristic).

### Strengths

### Issues (Critical / Important / Minor)

**Important — `useCancelRun` cache invalidation gap (the adjudicated item)**
`frontend/src/hooks/use-runs.ts:26-33` invalidates only `["runs"]`; `RunDetailPage.tsx:261,272-274` calls this same hook unmodified. The brief's interface note explicitly says cancel should invalidate `['run', id]` **and** `['runs']`. This is a real, named spec requirement, not an inferred one — the brief wrote out the exact query key. The impact is real: the detail page's own displayed status doesn't reflect "canceled" until the next poll tick (≤2.5 s) rather than immediately on mutation success, and while the cancel mutation is in flight the Cancel button stays enabled/interactive for that whole window (no immediate `isPending`-driven UI update tied to the detail query itself). It works out via polling because "canceled" is terminal and polling doesn't stop until the terminal state is *observed* — so this is self-correcting, but it is still a deviation from the explicit interface contract, not an equivalent alternative implementation of it.
**Verdict: Important, not Critical.** It's a spec deviation with a real (if small, ≤2.5s) user-facing effect, but it doesn't break anything, doesn't risk stuck polling, and the report proactively flagged it with correct reasoning — this is a "should fix before merge" item, not a blocker.
**Fix:** extend `useCancelRun` to also invalidate `["run", variables]` in its `onSuccess` (variables is the run id passed to `mutate`), e.g.:
```ts
onSuccess: (_data, id) =&gt; {
  void queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["runs"] });
  void queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["run", id] });
},
```
This is a one-line, zero-risk change to a shared hook and doesn't require `RunDetailPage` to fork its own cancel logic.

**Minor — Cancel button has no pending/loading text**
`RunDetailPage.tsx:311-318` disables the button via `disabled={cancelMutation.isPending}` but the label stays "Cancel" the whole time, giving no feedback that the click registered (compare to patterns elsewhere in the app that might swap label text, though I didn't find a strict local convention to compare against). Cosmetic only.

**Minor — `run.error` gating on `run.status === "failed"` combined with truthiness**
`RunDetailPage.tsx:322`: `run.status === "failed" &amp;&amp; run.error` means a failed run with a null/empty `error` renders no alert at all, which seems intentional (nothing to show) and matches the brief's phrasing ("`error` in a `role="alert"` when `status === "failed"`" — implicitly when there is an error to show). Not a bug, just worth noting it's an implicit interpretation rather than a literal one.

### Assessment

**Task quality:** Approved (with one recommended follow-up)

**Reasoning:** The implementation matches the brief's stated interfaces almost exactly — query key, polling predicate, rendered sections, artifact href construction (verified against the exact test-asserted nested-path string), 404/error/loading states, and route wiring are all correct and the tests genuinely exercise them via MSW rather than mocking around the logic. Code quality is clean: no `any`, no `instanceof File/Blob`, `artifactUrl` reused rather than hand-built, null-safe formatting throughout, accessible markup. The one real deviation from spec is the `useCancelRun` invalidation gap, which the implementer self-identified with accurate reasoning about impact and a concrete proposed fix. I rate this **Important** rather than Critical or a mere Minor: the brief was explicit about the query key to invalidate, so it's a genuine (if narrow, self-healing-within-2.5s) contract miss rather than a cosmetic nit — it should be fixed (one-line change to the shared hook) before this is considered fully spec-complete, but it does not block merging as-is since behavior is correct within one poll cycle and no state gets stuck.</result>

<result>Confirmed the blast radius. boltz2's required `sequences` is `type: object` with `additionalProperties` → `pickKind` returns `"json"` → not guided → collapsed Advanced. Same dead-end as ablang2. So **2 of the 3 real fixtures** (ablang2, boltz2) have their sole required input hidden in a collapsed panel with no visible error on submit. ---

**Verdict: Ship with nits** — the contracts, schema-engine validation/widget symmetry, auth seam, and no-`instanceof-File` guarantees all hold. There is one confirmed high-impact UX defect (required non-scalar fields render collapsed with no visible submit error) that I'd fix before real users hit ablang2/boltz2, but it does not corrupt data or break the antifold core loop the E2E proves. Calling it a strong nit rather than a hard blocker since it's server-safe and the primary demo tool works; if this branch is the first thing researchers touch with these tools, promote finding #1 to blocking.

### Blocking (must fix before merge) — none that corrupt data or break contracts; but read #1

**1. CONFIRMED — Required non-scalar fields are hidden in the collapsed Advanced panel, and their validation error is invisible → silent submit dead-end.** `src/lib/schema-form/fields/describe.ts:87-97` (`isGuided`) gates guided placement on `scalarKinds = {enum, file, text, textarea, number, boolean}`, deliberately excluding `json` and `string-array`. `SchemaForm.tsx:83` starts `advancedOpen=false` with no auto-open logic.
- **Failure scenario (traced against real fixtures):** For **ablang2** (required `sequences` = array-of-objects → `json` kind) and **boltz2** (required `sequences` = object → `json` kind) — i.e. 2 of the 3 shipped fixtures — a researcher opening the submit page sees a form with **no visible required inputs** above a Submit button. Clicking Submit: `parseJsonFields` skips the empty JSON text; `form.handleSubmit` runs the zod resolver, which flags the required `sequences` as missing; because there's an error, `onSubmit` is never invoked (no navigation), and the error is attached to a `FieldRenderer` that isn't mounted (Advanced collapsed) so **nothing is displayed**. The user is stuck with zero feedback. antifold works only because its lone required field is a `file` (which is in `scalarKinds`).
- **Why the green suite missed it:** `SchemaForm.tsx`/`SubmitPage.tsx` are only tested with antifold; ablang2/boltz2 are exercised only in `build-zod.test.ts` (validation, no rendering). The E2E likewise uses an antifold-shaped tool.
- **Fix (smallest):** make `isGuided` also guide required `json`/`string-array` fields — i.e. `return field.required` (any required field is guided) — or, alternatively, force `advancedOpen=true` on mount when any advanced field is required, and/or auto-expand Advanced when `form.formState.errors` intersects advanced field names on submit. The first is simplest and matches user intent ("show me what I must fill in").

### Non-blocking (should / nice) — with triage of the logged Minors

Fix-now (cheap, real correctness/UX):
- **Required `string-array` / `json` / `file` fields aren't enforced by client zod when empty** (CONFIRMED). `z.array(z.string())` accepts `[]`; `z.unknown()` (objects) accepts `undefined`; and JSON fields aren't registered so a required-but-empty object silently passes client validation and sends a payload missing the key. This is *acceptable* under "server-authoritative" (backend 422s), and `SubmitPage` renders 422 detail inline — so **defer is fine**, but pairs naturally with the #1 fix (once the field is visible, add `.min(1)`/`.nonempty()` or a required-JSON presence check for better UX). Low priority on its own.
- **Logged Minor — Advanced panel hardcoded `id="advanced-options-panel"`** (`SchemaForm.tsx:157/162`): only bites if two `SchemaForm`s mount (future comparison view). Cheap `useId()` fix; defer to Plan 10 unless a multi-form view is imminent.

Defer to Plan 10 / polish (agreed with ledger triage):
- **Theme toggle not persisted/initialized** (CONFIRMED via grep: no `localStorage`/`matchMedia`/`classList.add` bootstrap anywhere; `TopBar.tsx:26` reads `.contains("dark")` which is never set on load). Dark mode resets every reload and the initial icon can mismatch. Cosmetic; defer.
- **Post-login redirect drops `search`/`hash`** (`RequireAuth.tsx:22` stores `location`, but `LoginPage.tsx:39` reads only `from.pathname`). Deep links with query strings lose them. Defer unless deep-linking matters.
- **Number inputs lack `min`/`max` HTML hints** (Zod enforces; `describe`'s `schema` field is computed and unused). UX hint only; defer.
- **Form error `&lt;p&gt;` not wired via `aria-describedby`** (only `description` is; `aria-invalid` is set). a11y polish; defer.
- **Stale `frontend/README.md`** (Vite/Oxlint boilerplate) and **`components.json` `baseColor:"zinc"`** vs slate palette — doc/config-only; defer. README is worth a 1-line fix since it actively misinforms (says Oxlint; project uses ESLint).
- **`artifactUrl` doesn't encode `runId`** (`api.ts:1308`) — runId is a server-issued UUID, not user-controlled; harmless. Defer.
- **&gt;500 kB bundle advisory** → Plan 10 code-split, as planned.
- **Very-new majors** (React19/Vite8/TS6/ESLint10/Vitest4) — monitor; not actionable now.

Additional emergent observations (not in the ledger):
- **`src/components/ui/sonner.tsx` is dead code** (CONFIRMED): it's the only importer of `next-themes`, it's never mounted (no `&lt;Toaster/&gt;` in the tree), and `toast()` is never called. It's a generated `ui/*` primitive (excluded from the review diff), so not a branch defect — but `next-themes` and `sonner` are shipped deps with zero live usage. Either wire up a `&lt;Toaster/&gt;` (would improve the currently silent mutation failures) or drop the dep in a cleanup. Non-blocking.
- **Mutation errors on `RunsPage` cancel/delete are swallowed** (PLAUSIBLE UX gap): `useCancelRun`/`useDeleteRun` have no `onError`, and `RunsPage` only disables buttons while pending — a failed cancel/delete shows nothing. Consistent with the "no toast wired" observation above. Defer, but a good candidate once Sonner is mounted.

### Verified strengths
- **Contract consistency (traced, clean):** query keys `['me']`/`['tools']`/`['tool',id]`/`['runs']`/`['run',id]` are used identically across `use-auth`, `use-tools`, `use-runs`, `SubmitPage`, `RunDetailPage`, `TopBar`, `LoginPage`. Routes match the spec exactly (`App.tsx`). The multipart submit (`tool_id` + `params` JSON + `files`) is built once in `api.ts:submitRun` and asserted byte-for-byte in `api.test.ts`; `SchemaForm.onSubmit({values,files})` → `SubmitPage` → `submitRun` is wired consistently; `artifactUrl`/`isTerminal` used identically in list + detail. Cancel correctly invalidates both `['runs']` and `['run',id]` (the logged fix).
- **Schema engine validation ↔ widget symmetry (traced):** `unwrapNullable` is logically identical in `build-zod.ts` and `describe.ts`; both unwrap `anyOf:[T,null]` the same way and treat scalar-item arrays (`string-array`/`z.array(scalar)`) vs object-item arrays and objects (`json`/`z.array(unknown)`/`unknown`) identically. Enum detection is identical. I found no field kind that validates one way and renders another — the divergence is *placement* (finding #1), not kind mapping.
- **Auth seam (traced):** `RequireAuth` shows a live-region loader while `['me']` resolves and only renders `&lt;Outlet/&gt;` after — no protected fetch fires before auth resolves (child pages mount only inside the guard). Logout clears the `['me']` cache (`setQueryData(['me'], null)` + invalidate) and navigates to `/login`; `retry:false` on `useAuth` means a 401 fails fast to redirect. Tests cover authed/unauthed/redirect.
- **No `instanceof File`/`Blob` anywhere** (CONFIRMED via grep of all `src/` incl. `ui/*` and `e2e/`): the only match is an explanatory comment in `FileField.tsx`. Files are tracked via `FileList`/structural handling and a `filesRef` map — robust against the jsdom/native `File` swap. No `any` in non-test source; the one unavoidable type bridge (zodResolver ↔ FieldValues in `SchemaForm.tsx:60`) is narrowly scoped and documented.
- Client Zod is correctly treated as UX-only everywhere; `SubmitPage.messageForError` surfaces server 422/429 detail inline, honoring server authority.

Net: the architecture is sound and the contracts are tight. Finding #1 is the one thing I'd resolve (one-line `isGuided` change) before researchers touch ablang2/boltz2; everything else is safely deferrable polish.</result>

### Spec Compliance — ✅

- ✅ [src/fold_at_scripps/api/admin.py:69-88] `GET /admin/runs/{run_id}/artifacts/{artifact_path:path}` added to the `/admin` router, inherits router-level `require_admin` (admin.py:50) — no route-level override.

- ✅ Traversal guard: `outputs = storage.outputs_dir(run_id).resolve()` computed **before** `target = (outputs / artifact_path).resolve()`, then `not target.is_relative_to(outputs) or not target.is_file()` → 404. Confirmed `outputs_dir()` returns a possibly-relative path (`storage_root` defaults to `"./data"`), so `.resolve()` is load-bearing for `is_relative_to` correctness, and it's resolved on the correct (parent) side first.
- ✅ Imports added: `FileResponse` from `fastapi.responses`, `Storage`/`get_storage` from `fold_at_scripps.storage`. No `actor`/audit dependency — correct for a read-only action (matches existing pattern: `admin_run_detail` also has no actor/audit; only mutating `admin_cancel` does).
- ✅ No route conflict: Starlette's default converter for `{run_id}` is the string type, which does not match `/`, so `/runs/{run_id}` cannot accidentally consume the multi-segment `/runs/{run_id}/artifacts/...` path. New route sits between `admin_run_detail` and `admin_cancel` with no ambiguity.
- ✅ Byte-for-byte identical traversal/membership/FileResponse logic vs. the researcher `download_artifact` in `api/runs.py:129-149`; only the run resolver and the (correctly dropped) `user` param differ.
- ✅ Tests match brief: admin downloads alice's artifact → 200/`HELLO`; unknown artifact → 404. `_tmp_storage_root` is autouse, sets `FOLD_STORAGE_ROOT` via `monkeypatch.setenv`, clears `get_settings` cache before and after — true mirror of `tests/api/test_runs.py`'s existing fixture, writes only to `tmp_path`, no repo leakage.
- ✅ Global constraints: `from __future__ import annotations` present, type hints on all params/return (`-&gt; FileResponse`), Google-style one-line docstring, absolute imports, no bare except, line lengths within 100, `ruff check`/`format --check` reported clean, full suite green (159 passed) per report (not re-run, per instructions).

### Strengths

- **Partial-update correctness is real, not just claimed.** `buildChanges()` (`UsersPage.tsx:296-305`) diffs each of the three fields against the original `user` prop and only includes changed keys in the `AdminUserUpdate` object — verified by reading the logic line-by-line, not just trusting the report.
- Clean re-sync of form state: `resetForm()` runs on every dialog open (`handleOpenChange`), so stale edits or post-invalidation fresh data are correctly reflected next time the dialog opens.
- Error path is sound: mutation failure leaves the dialog open (no `onSuccess` fires) so the admin can correct/retry, while the hook's `onError` still toasts.
- Native `&lt;select&gt;` choice is well-justified and narrowly scoped: only the two enum fields in the edit form use it; the token dialog and other inputs remain shadcn primitives (`Input`, `Dialog`, `Button`, `Label`), and it's styled to visually match (`SELECT_CLASS` mirrors the shadcn input surface classes).
- Good accessibility hygiene: `useId()` + `htmlFor` pairing throughout, `sr-only` table caption, `role="status"`/`aria-live` on the loading state (pre-existing component, reused correctly).
- Consistent with existing repo idioms (`void refetch()` pattern for `ErrorState.onRetry`, `React.FormEvent` used as a bare type reference without an explicit import, matching `CatalogPage.tsx`).
- No `any`, no `instanceof File/Blob` misuse, no lint suppressions.

### Issues

**Minor** — `frontend/src/pages/admin/UsersPage.tsx:330-356` (native `&lt;select&gt;` vs. shadcn `Select`): as anticipated in the report, this is a visual/component-library inconsistency (two different focus-ring/border implementations for "the same kind of control" elsewhere in the admin UI), not a functional or accessibility defect. Justified by the `userEvent.selectOptions` test contract, which cannot drive a Radix combobox. Acceptable tradeoff; flagging only so a future task doesn't diverge further without the same justification.

**Minor** — `frontend/src/pages/admin/UsersPage.tsx:300` — `Number(quota)` on a non-empty string; if a user manages to produce a non-numeric string in the number input (e.g. via paste, or transient states like `"-"`), this could yield `NaN`, which would satisfy `nextQuota !== user.max_concurrent_runs_override` and send `max_concurrent_runs_override: NaN` (serializes to `null` in `JSON.stringify`, silently changing the intended semantics). Low risk given native `type="number"` browser input constraints and no evidence of a real-world path to trigger it in this admin-only screen; not worth blocking on.

**Verdict:** Ship it

The branch is clean, internally consistent, and the one security-sensitive addition (the admin artifact endpoint) is correct. Nothing blocks merge. Details below, most-severe first.

### Blocking (must fix before merge)
None. All four focus areas verified with the source traced, not just the diff.

### Non-blocking — triage of the logged Minors

- **`errorMessage` duplicated in 6 files** (5 admin hooks + `use-runs.ts`) — CONFIRMED. Defer. Identical 1-line body (`error instanceof ApiError ? error.detail : "Something went wrong"`); a shared `lib/errors.ts` helper is a trivial polish-pass extraction, not a correctness issue. Fits the "Plan 10 polish" bucket.
- **Users edit `Number(quota)` → NaN → JSON null** (`UsersPage.tsx:2385`) — CONFIRMED but very low risk. The input is `type="number"` so the browser blocks non-numeric entry; the only path to a bad value is edge locale/paste behavior, and the failure mode (silently clearing the override) is recoverable via re-edit. Optional `Number.isFinite` guard if the file is touched. Defer.
- **Settings Save fires PATCH even with no changes** — CONFIRMED. `buildChanges` returns `{}` and `adminUpdateSettings({})` still fires. Harmless (server no-ops, `exclude_unset` means empty body) but produces a spurious "Settings saved" toast + audit-log noise. Nice-to-have no-op guard; defer, but flag it since it writes an audit entry on a non-change.
- **Native `&lt;select&gt;` vs shadcn Select** — CONFIRMED, intentional (testability via `userEvent.selectOptions`), styled to match. Accept as-is per the brief.
- **No cancel-flow / status-filter interaction tests on admin Runs** — CONFIRMED coverage gap. The cancel *hook* is tested and the detail page renders the dialog; the button-to-mutation wiring is untested. Defer (brief didn't require it), but worth a follow-up ticket.

### Verified strengths

- **Backend endpoint security (Task 0) — the critical item, fully traced.** `src/fold_at_scripps/api/admin.py:205-224` is the shipped researcher endpoint (`api/runs.py:129-149`) with exactly one substitution: owner-scoped `get_run(session, user, run_id)` → owner-unscoped `admin_get_run(session, run_id)`. All four guards are intact and identical to the proven code: (1) router-level `require_admin` gates the route — no non-admin can reach it; (2) membership check — `artifact_path` must match an entry in `run.artifacts`; (3) traversal guard — `outputs` and `target` both `.resolve()`d *before* `is_relative_to(outputs)`, so `../` escapes 404 rather than serving; (4) `is_file()` check. `outputs_dir(run_id)` is the correct per-run base (`run_root/outputs`). No path outside a run's own outputs is reachable.
- **Contract consistency across all six screens — verified by count.** Every admin query key is namespaced `['admin', …]`; every admin mutation pairs `invalidateQueries` on its key + `toast.success` on success and `toast.error(errorMessage(err))` on error. `useAdminCancelRun` correctly double-invalidates `['admin','runs']` + `['admin','run',id]`.
- **`adminArtifactUrl` (not `artifactUrl`) on the admin run detail — CONFIRMED.** `AdminRunDetailPage.tsx:1010` uses `adminArtifactUrl(runId, artifact.path)` → `/admin/runs/{id}/artifacts/…`, and the test asserts the exact href. This is the whole point of Task 0 and it's wired correctly; other users' artifacts will resolve through the admin-gated endpoint, not 404.
- **Guard/routing.** `RequireAdmin` redirects non-admins to `/` (with a loading state to avoid flash-redirect during auth resolution); every `/admin/*` route nests under it. Researcher/public routes are untouched. `&lt;Toaster/&gt;` mounted once at `App` root.
- **Toast retrofit is safe.** `use-runs.ts` diff *adds* only `onError` blocks — the 9a `onSuccess` invalidations (`useCancelRun`→`['runs']`+`['run',id]`; `useDeleteRun`→`['runs']`) are preserved verbatim, with a regression test covering both error paths.
- **`instanceof File`/`Blob`: zero** (grep confirmed). **`any` type: zero** — every diff hit is the English word in a comment/docstring, not a type annotation. `AdminRunRead.params` uses `Record&lt;string, unknown&gt;`, correctly narrowed at the render boundary in `formatParamValue`.

No emergent cross-screen defects (no missing invalidation, no toast rendering a raw object — `errorMessage` always coerces to a string). Ready to open the PR.</result>
